Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards, do on both legs two cauterizations in each leg at the tip of the knife finger; and let the cauterization be long, one under the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauterizations open for a long time without curing, until the fluid comes out; afterwards cure with the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	It seems like we've reached the end of this text.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the belly comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retentive and digestive virtues that are in the stomach and intestine are dulled, and cannot be cured by any methods of treatment; and you see the patient very suffering and strong virtue, then do a great cautery on the stomach according to what was spoken about the stomach cautery, at the cauterization of the veins; and four cauterizations around the mouth subtle to all one subtle cauterization hook, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistors abundant and the patient suffering, then do a cauterization on the elbow, and one cauterization on each thigh, and two small cauterizations on the stomach near the large one, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When the hemorrhoids are at the fundament, one or more, and are ancient and of cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit, then do cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that which is entirely behind the almecdate pouch and pouch in a triangle, and one cauterization under the mouth. two must be done.
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that the stomach is chilled, and the meat does not cook, and we see the face inflamed, then do a great cauterization on the stomach, as it was said before, and another one on the liver, and another one on the spleen with the entire hook-like cautery; and let the cautery stay for a long time. After that, cure the patient until he is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	It seems I've been diving into medieval medical texts!
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the hump, if it bleeds the cautery that looks like a razor, and then put it all ablaze on the top of the hump that is cut; and I leave your hand as long as the cautery reaches the birthplace of the vein, from which the blood flows. Do this once or twice, and if there is much hump, cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards treat with ointments that are beneficial until they are healed; and if you cauterize a great cautery on the hump, it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	a badly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will tell in its place, such an illness comes that can not be healed except by cauterizing.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a fistula comes and is inflamed and spews forth corrupt and moist purulence, you should try to probe it as deeply as possible, and keep track of how deep it has gone. Afterwards cauterize the cautery that looks like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the depth that the probe has entered, and continue to cauterize until the corrupt flesh is burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to the severity of the case; and be careful not to burn the nerve that are nearby, and the large vessels. If the fistula extends into the bladder and intestine, be careful of these places, and do not do this except in a secure location, and think that it is not a miracle; afterwards treat the place until it is healed, and if the place has been cut open, and the purulence has been removed for a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the purulence has not been removed, know that the place is infected, and corrupting the flesh at its core; and thus as one of those things that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of frost comes to the kidneys and there is a large swelling, and it does not take on the shape of a woman's womb, then you should cauterize it over the kidneys from one side with a cautery needle, and from the other side with a spatula-like cautery that we have mentioned before; and if we cauterize in between, there will be three cauteries in line, and they will make more great aid.
de la vessie	the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is weak and soft from frost and moisture, and the patient retains urine, then you should cauterize in the part of the back above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, one on the right and one on the left, each being as long as a thumb's length; and you should do one cautery behind the back, or two if you need it; and make the cauteries like a spade, according to the form mentioned before.
de la marris	the womb (or uterus)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and does not allow conception to take place, and the menstrual flowers are corrupt and their ends are delayed; and when they come, a great pain is felt: then it is necessary to make three cauterizations around the belly, as we have said for the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and make the cauterizations like a spade, as we have said.
de la hainche	the hip (or navel)
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist and viscous substances descend to the hip bone, and because of this the patient moves out of their place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the abscess is found at the junction of the two bones, then you should cauterize the sick person above the hip bone with one cautery resembling a circle, and mark in front of the abscess around the bone as it curves, so that the bone is inside the circle; and make the cauteries like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizations are not available to you, then make three large cauterizations of the olive-like shape, and make them as deep as all the other cauterizations; and let it heal until it is sound. (Note: "olivaire grans" refers to a type of cautery instrument that resembles an olive)
de la dolor de la hainche	the pain of the hip (or loins)
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the breast of the groin, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient has been treated for what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purify the patient with thick foul-smelling pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After that, make it burn; and the way to burn is according to two manners: that is to say, together with burning medicines, and burning by fire. Burning by fire is according to many manners, among which one is such that you burn three triangular cauteries on top of the breast of the groin, in this shape, and I make a good depth and large, and there be between each cauter a space as wide as a thumb, and the cauters are olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cauter in the middle above the head of the groin, so that there are four in this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cauterization does not reach the circular cauter that we have spoken of before in the dislocation of the groin; but do it in this manner that the circles contain all the groin, and all the fat of the skin is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the manner in which they do in sciatica, when the pain stays in the groin and does not reach as far as the thigh or the leg. And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, then you make two cauterizations there where the patient says that the pain stays, and one cauterization above the ankle three fingers' breadth to the left side; and the cauters are knife-shaped, and burn the thick layer of skin; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as the toe or near it, then you cauterize where he feels the pain three finger's breadth or four at the point called "point".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, you make more of them; and if he knows that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, then you cauterize at the cutellary or circular point, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not burn too little so as to leave the nerves and great arteries intact, and that you do not make more trouble and contraction for the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	Et j'ai même vu des personnes qui ont fait cauteriser au-dessus du pied, et ils les avaient brûlées si profondément que la jambe entière était enflée, et le pied aussi, et a fini par se pourrir et s'empirer tout le pied. Après une maladie de ventre qui leur a fait mourir.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cautery on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is entirely red and smells strongly, and then put it on the crotch of the sick hag, and turned over on the sound side; and cauterize once .i. cautery again and let him leave .iij. days; and then make a poultice with butter, and let the wound stay open for a long time; after the ointment cure until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasin says that we should use a patch of this cauterizer for the fear of his sight, and see who uses it; and yet those are good cauterizers which can bear it, and the place where it takes effect.
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or percussion or from too great evacuation, or from seeming expansion of cold matter, none of these appearances is worth cauterizing except that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after these that the sick person be freed from fetid pills or other appearances, and that one make signs on their back, at the place where the pain holds, three lines signed with ink, and in each line .v. cauterizations or more according to virtue and quantity that the sick person can bear; and let the cauterizations be made according to the cautery called "point"; and if you see it, make .iij. cauterizations or .iiij. at the middle point of the cautery in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have stiffened limbs when they wake up, and pain; and you find in the lower back of the spine and on the appearance that comes over the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you know how to cure it, then cauterize at the point of the cautery in this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	If the cautery is to be done on each part of the spine equally. And if you see, cauterize around the spine with a cautery that pricks two or three lines deep, and have the points close together. After the cure, let it heal until it is sound according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply cautery near the gallbladder which is in danger of being damaged by nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of the joints is from a swelling that is spread to each member of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, which they call "podagre" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, then it is cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and have the cauteries olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then make a cautery to the full extent of the point. And when the pains come up to the knee and the other joints, and this happens many times, then make a cautery above each kneecap three cauteries or four from each part, to the full olive-shaped length; and if you need more, then make more, but do not hold your hand farther than the span of the cure is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knee and the back, then administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make pricks around the wrist bone two lines deep; and if there remains no pain in the thumbs, make pricks on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the sides or to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and do good governance for the sick person and give medicines. For if you give good governance and purge phlegm, they will be made sound with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	It seems like you've switched to a new text about a different medical condition.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When a rupture comes on suddenly, and the intestines descend to the groin and this is new, then you must not cut it that day; and have him eat things that ease the belly, so that the faeces descend from his belly; afterwards make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to lift his loin until the swelling is repaired, and clean them with your fingers, and sign of an incision below the rupture above the bone of the elbow, and draw a mark like half a circle over the body; then heat the cautery with which this form is made:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and he lets out sounds. Then clean the intestines to their place; and the attendants make a sign with his hand that they will not return behind; and work well the thighs of the patient, and put under him one cushion and one sergeant over the thighs, and another over the chest which holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign all your hand, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you come to the bone; and take care carefully that the intestines do not burst when you make the cautery; that you will not burn him; and that through this the patient will not die or get worse.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you don't reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are in vain. Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, if he is given a well-made belt, and it is worn for another 40 days; and have good rest, so that he does not exert himself too much and avoid excessive consumption of drinking and eating, and loud shouting; and when he has followed this instruction, he will be completely healed. And I will explain the cure of cutting in his chapter after this.

de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any member, whether from a fall or an injury, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery called "point", and let the cauterization be according to the length of the member, its size, its fragility, and its virtue, and its location of twists and of pain. If it is healed from the first cauterization, well; if not, repeat another cauterization over that one, because that custom is that it must change in the member that is nearest to it, so that you do the cauterizations until the illness is healed.
de meselerie	It seems like we've switched to a different topic!
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The patients are aided once with cautery for great help, and namely the disease that comes from putrefaction of bile and melancholy. When you see it being cauterized, beware if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not remain nor disappear, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then do five cauteries on the head: one on the forehead, and the other towards the front at the end of the eyebrows; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and leave your hand so that the cauterizes come just to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can come out; and cauterize on the mouse according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the inflammation is scattered everywhere and it shows clearly, you must do the cauterizes of these five on the head that we have said, and one cauterize under the nape, and two cauterizes on the spine of the neck, and six cauterizes on the spine of the back, and one large one on the groin and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the thigh, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, so you do not burn them; and once make a cauterize on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more cauteries I make, the more help it brings and the greater is the profit; and know that the sick person does not feel pain at the cauterization if the healthy ones do, because the body is already entirely corrupted. And it is necessary that the cauterizations be big and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.
de enfleure	To inflate.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When an inflammation comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then one makes cauterizations on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be a bit entering into the depth of the wound; then treat it with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes one makes a cauterization at the tip of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the inflammation goes away; but otherwise no one should intervene if he is not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	of boils
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has developed and the remedy of medicine is no longer useful, then one cauterizes it with a cautery a bit deep, according to the size of the boil, until the abscess is removed and its color changes; then treat it with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of chicken and blood of eel, each part equally; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and let it breathe in the air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for syphilis (chancre) through cauterization.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the chancre comes at the beginning, and you look at it to stop it, if you cauterize it with a fire cauter that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the chancre. And wise men have said that one should also make a cauter in the middle of the chancre; but I do not think this is good, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen this happen once before; and the most direct thing is to cauterize around it with a cauter that is called "circle", as we have said about many cauters.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the swelling which cannot move
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease that is called "adubelati", and it takes time to heal or because of the superfluity it makes or because of the age of the patient when they are decrepit (that is, too old) and they have pus in their veins, or because of the season; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize around with many small cauters that are painful; after that leave it alone. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing all through the cauter, then heat the cauter whose shape is like this:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cauter has pierced the core, and the cauters be such that the patient feels them throughout in this way that the flow of the pus is alleviated. Then cure him as long as he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment with fire by iron (i.e., a heated iron or cauter)
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another manner of disease is called "corrodens", and it's nothing but gangrene of a member, because it consumes the members just like fire consumes dry wood. If you see this disease in a place where fire can be applied, then heat many small and large cauters together according to what is needed for that place, then cauterize all around until you exhaust all the corruption and nothing remains of it, except for whatever was corrupted being removed. And then let it be for three days, and apply ointments to the cauterized places so that they can heal with a crust, as long as the fire's scorchings are removed and all the corruption is gone. After that, treat them with medicinal oils that generate flesh. And if after three days healthy skin does not appear, it's good; and if not, then reapply the cauter to what remains of the corrupted places. This gangrene has been cured sometimes with medicine alone instead of fire, but nonetheless fire is a greater aid, and I have already said in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the little splinters that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often times it happens that the feet outdoors get a disease called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a large, hardened thing that hurts the foot. And the ulcer of this disease is in two ways. That is to say, fire cauterization, and hot water cauterization. Fire cauterization is when you heat up one cauterizer like a horse shoe nail, and make it out of good iron to the size that it can pierce the callus from all sides, and have subtle edges; then put it hot on top of the callus, and turn your hand completely around the callus until it comes to the temperature of the callus; and leave it for three days until it starts to rot; then make a poultice with bitter gall mixed with oil, and let the poultice be on top of the whole thing all night, and the callus will fall off and the roots will be pulled out. Then cure the place with ointment melting fat until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are converted into the body outdoors and it happens many times in hands and on feet, it is necessary that you bring hot water cauterization; and it is in this manner: take a copper or iron container, or a horse shoe nail, and put it on top of the boil and the scab, which is to say little splinters; and put the container on so that it can pierce all around, then put a small amount of hot water in it, and hold your hand tight, and press your hand while turning so that the edges of the container come to the root of the boil, and the hot water can penetrate deep enough to reach the root; and let the patient suffer the cauterization of the hot water for one hour; then leave it alone, and it will pull out all its roots. Thus do another after that, until you have extracted all those in the body, and then cure them with ointments that melt fat.
li cure dou trembler	Li cure dou trembler (The Cure for Shaking)
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some person shakes with cold or quartan fever or another, you should make him four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cauterization between each spine; and one on the belly and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped cauterization; he will let him shake and he will hasten to health from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	pustulous blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	At no time appear on the body blisters or pustules that come from gross corrupt matter. If it is necessary when they first appear to make a cauterization over each head of the blister: a fine cauterization of mistletoe wood, whose point was grasped by fire, or of aristolochus root length, or lentil-shaped cauterization. And at no time should we cauterize them from the beginning when they appear, in this manner, but rather are the superfluities that come from them burst and healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is severed
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times great hemorrhages of blood come from the artery that is severed at the wound that appears first, or at the incision of the aposteme, or from the cauterization of the member, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to staunch them.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to anyone, if you hasten to place your index finger on the wound and press it hard until the bleeding stops beneath your finger, and no more drops come out; then put several small and large olive-shaped cauterizers in the fire until they are all red; then take one, either big or little depending on the wound and its location where the artery runs, and place the cauterizer on that vein while holding your finger there, and hold the cauterizer so that the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spouts out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauterizer is extinguished, then take another one hastily from those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do these things one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other malady comes on the sick person; and know that when blood runs from an artery, it cannot be well staunched directly when the artery is large, unless it is done by one of the four methods that we have said: or by cauterization, or by extraction if it has not been cut, or by strongly tying a thread, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and strained accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who would remind that staunching by tightly tying with a cloth or by applying hot things on top, or similar methods, is not beneficial if it does not provide relief.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and he does not have a surgeon or medicine present, then he should put his index finger on the wound of the vein as we said, and press it well until it is stopped above the wound and the vein; and do not move the finger, but moisten it with cold water often as it can be very cold until the bleeding is frozen and thickened and stopped; and make an inquiry in advance for cauterizers and medicines of which he may have need.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical remedies.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all illness where it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or hot medicine, and the reasons and causes and instruments and forms of cauterizations; and I placed that chapter at the beginning up to this point, and I will go on in this chapter by the same route so that you may find what you want more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, dear son, you must learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterizations, and therefore it is necessary to take greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there are many times evacuation of blood when opening the vein, and incising over an abscess, and treating wounds, and extracting thorns, and incising over the bone, and similar things; or there is danger and fear, and death comes to many.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you that you should not be foolish. For many types of people come to cures. Some come who are so attached to their illness that they would die easily for the foolishness that they find in their disease, and from the greatness of their wickedness; and of these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these there are those who give you their sense, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the disease is spiteful. It's not necessary that you consent to those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great caution in your honor than in your avarice, and do not open foolishly but wisely what you are certain of, and from which you can take and reap reward; and use prognosis and indication in the care of your patients towards whom salvation may be converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to be guided by the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen. (This is a closing prayer, likely written in Old French, and it seems to conclude the chapter with a pious sentiment.)
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered you this chapter by dividing it into sections, as is before the chapter on cauterizations, which I previously explained to you from head to foot, so that you may find more easily what you will need. (This is a concluding remark, likely written in Old French, and it seems to indicate that the author has organized the content of this chapter for easier reference.)
dou chief plein d’aigue	Filled with water (or possibly "full of wisdom", but "dough chef plein d'aigue" is a literal translation). This phrase appears to be a concluding remark, possibly indicating that the author has provided enough information or that the chapter is complete.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Understand that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the cord is pulled too tightly on the child's head; and sometimes it comes from a cause unknown to us.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease outside of children, and in all those that I have seen it has come on quickly to death; and for that reason it seems to me that it is not worth much effort to treat such cases.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose eyes were full of water, and the head was swelling every day so much that it couldn't be held up; and I thought the child was dead, and this condition is caused by an abscess gathered under the bone above the temple, between the skull and the bone; and the treatment is such that if the abscess is between the skull and the bone, and the pustules are small, you make a cut in the head through which the pus can drain, making it as long as two fingers, so that the pus can run out; behold the shape of the incision:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If moisture is more abundant, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and the signs you see are the corners of the head parted from each other on both sides, and the sharpness jumps out when you press it with your hand from inside, and this is not relieved: then you must make three incisions within the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision take out all the moisture. Then close the incisions with cloth and powders, and put vinegar and oil on them, and leave it in this state until the fifth day; then release the dislocation, and treat the wound by stitches and ointments, and let the head be strained equally, and give the patient dry meat of poultice or moist sores as long as the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look and see the position of the large abscess and the assembly of the sharpness; because sometimes it is in front, sometimes at the back, sometimes to the right, and sometimes to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut at the spot where the abscess opens and the filling of the sharpness is located, and make an incision according to what you can see; and be careful not to cut the artery; and if there is bleeding from the blood vessel, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.

Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease called "catarre" in the arm or leg, and the disease is old, and medicine treatment does not help, then the last cure is cauterization with those things that will cut off both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then, when you see them to be cut off, the patient must bend their head back; after that, rub the place with a rough cloth until the arteries show; then take the patient's neck in one cloth and pull hard; then look where the vein breaks, and the spot of both is near the ears, and the flesh is restored; then mark the spots with ink, then cut off both with a sharp spatula to the depth of two parts, so that the edge comes up to the bone, and let it be by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see fit, push the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting in the same way as two threads across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will shoot up continuously out of it.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery doesn't bleed at first, you should measure three fingers deep and mark with ink, then cut up to the bone; and what is necessary for the blood to flow out is 7-8 threads, and maybe a little more or less depending on how much the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery. Then look at the wound: if there's pus remaining on top of the bone, you should cut it off so that no abscesses remain, then drain the wound and bind it up, and treat with ointment until it is healed.

Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from those wounds are descending over the face of the head and do not benefit from any medicine that is done there, and you see the face of the sick person becoming red and hot like fever; and the eyelids are tight and moist so that the hair of the eyebrows is down, and the eyebrows are scalded by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary for this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	They would call the ancient "cure for a bruise", and it is that you do to the patient who has this illness: let him have long hair on his forehead; then make three incisions on his forehead evenly according to its length; and one of the incisions be as two does in between the eyebrows going down just up to the nose, and the other two be two inches at the sides above the eyelids, and take care to avoid cutting into the arteries that are on the sides above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the jaws, and each wound should be three finger-widths across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and you should have prepared a piece of sponge and wrung out the cloth to absorb the blood, then tie the sponge tightly on either side with it is this shape:

And place the sharp edge towards the fatty part of the skin, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and push it in until it reaches the first cut. dou reume des eulz	the water of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When one comes accustomed to a strong catarrh, and you see the eyes become dim and small, and weaken the vision, and the eyelids are burned; and the hair is falling out, and the head in front is very painful, and the patient is coughing; then know by these signs that those materials and the catarrh come from many voices, and the mother of the disease, which cures it if it exists, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And then command the patient to run their forehead, and make a large incision in front of the nose, and another one a inch deep. And begin from the incision at the left temple to the right temple, and be the incision just up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move towards the mouth; and when the bone is uncovered, squeeze out all the blood into an sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the incision with old cotton, and a linen thread. Then bind on top with damp cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be careful not to get a hot abscess; when it's removed, you should scrape the bone until flesh begins to sprout, then cure it with caustic substances that cause flesh to form.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All the things that fall into ears are one of the four things: or grains, such as wheat, barley, beans; or beast, like fish, birds; or stone from a mine or similar thing, like iron; or seeds, such as peas, lentils.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something like a stone or another kind of thing that does not belong in the ear falls into it and does not grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun. This cure often works many times; and if it does not come out, try an extraction with subtle forceps; which is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the forceps, that's good; if not, try an extraction with a thin needle of small double thread; and if it does not come out that way, make a string of silver wire and insert one end into the ear canal tightly, and plug what is around the string with soft wax so that the blood cannot enter along with the string; then pull it out firmly, because many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this way, take bird's glue and place any instrument that can be made sharp for this purpose into the glue, and put some cotton around it; then press the glue over the stone or whatever it is, and pull it out.
