And the patient will feel it inside, and the distillation should be a small cup warmed over the fire so that it can be distilled in the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the stopping up of the ears.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a perforation in their ears; and the same thing happens to humans through blocking up a wound or boil inside the ear, and this blockage sometimes goes deep into the ear, so you can't see it; and sometimes there is a small hole left by the perforation, and you can see it clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, the one that goes deep and can't be seen is from a severe inflammation in several positions, and for the one that you can see, you should put the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see a scab formation, then the work has all the characteristics of this form.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be cut and scraped on both the front and back of the skin, without harming the ear; if the scab is a boil or pus in the ear, then take with your fine tweezers and carefully pick at it, until all the pus is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the scab is deep in the ear, then take a fine scraper and heat it slightly over the fire, then put it on the affected part of the ear. If you feel the scab with the pain that the sick person feels, prick it lightly, but be careful not to harm the eardrum; then put a plug into the ear according to the width of the perforation, and fill it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or you take a plug and fill it with rose water, and powder made from vitriol, and if you see the ear swelling, it's necessary that you remove the plug and put in another moistened plug made of cerote, which is made from red oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the discharge becomes bloody, then plunge a sponge into cold water and wring it out, and apply it to the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bloodstaining, such as treating with distilled waters.
de la char des papieres	Je pense que c'est un titre ou une mention qui marque la fin du texte médical, et que la phrase suivante est en fait le début d'un nouveau texte. Le terme "papieres" pourrait faire référence à un type de traitement ou d'application utilisant des papiers ou des feuilles pour quelque chose, mais sans plus de contexte, il est difficile de savoir exactement à quoi cela renvoie.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Je pense avoir compris maintenant ! Les "papieres" font référence à des feuilles ou des lamelles qui se trouvent dans les oreilles, en particulier lorsque les glandes du cerumène (ou "eulz") sont en activité et produisent une substance visqueuse.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if they are not incised, then let the cautery do a small lenticular cautery on it, and after the incision, it moves well; and many times repair, without any thing remaining from their roots; and when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times they come in paper, those things that seem like hail in their shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "grandine", and it is a gathering of moist grains on the upper and lower paper; the task is as follows: take care if the grandine moves from one side to the other, and it's a light thing to know; then make it large, then scrape off each part lightly, then take it to the pincers, and cut it. If you can't cut it without piercing a little the paper, don't harm anything to the patient; and if the crack is big, sew it with a suture, and cure it until it is healed; and if it's small, do nothing to it, because the ointments will restore it quickly and heal the skin.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grandine is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper over, and take the grandine to a pair of pincers, and cut and press it from one side to the other; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it doesn't harm anything; and when the grandine is cut, pour vinegar on the ear, and cure the place where the skin heals itself until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	It looks like we're switching to a different medical condition.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a grease that is dripped onto paper tissues above, and this happens more in children than in adults, and it causes great pain to their eyes, and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush into their eyes; and for this reason they lie on their faces often and sleep on them, and their paper tissues are under their eyelids moistened by the exinach that appears in the eye. And when you press the place with your thumbs and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of working is that the patient puts their head in your hand; and then take one linen cloth, and set up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of exinach contained in each part, then put it on them; and press with your thumbs from both sides so that the exinach is assembled inside the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the spatula cutting a slit of a size not greater than the wound made in the vein of the animal; and make the skin to be cut so far as you will come to the exinach; and in various dispositions the exinach comes out from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take it out and make it into one piece of cloth, pinching it between your thumbs on the outside; and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to add anything to the incision, so that you don't come all the way up to the spatula blade to the eye, so as not to cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exinach does not appear at the beginning of the incision, then enlarge the incision slightly until it appears; then take it out as we have said, then wet linen in oil and water, and put it on the place, and take it out from the bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who burn thread and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains; then they heal it until it is cured. And if an abscess or a hot lump comes up, they treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs grow into the skin and cause inflammation, and they harm themselves, and bring about unpleasant ways of illness such as constant tears and softening of the papers and swellings, until it is a cause of destruction of the skin; and the treatment is in four manners: either by cauterizing together with fire, or by medicine that stings according to what is written before or in the chapter on cauterization, and it is done by incision and stitching or by threads, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should put the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper from the eye with your left hand; if it is turned, it is good; if not, you should insert a needle into each thread on top and so that it is close to the edge of the paper where the hairs are growing, and pull up all the threads to the top of the paper, and turn it under the razor; then make an incision in the part underneath the paper, beneath the hairs that have grown together, cutting out all the scabby spots, from the large sore to the small one; then extract the thread, and put a small tent of cotton and fabric over the paper, then sew on top of the paper a figure like the calyx of a myrtle leaf, and in any case it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you see the paper rise which has been divided in two.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if you have to deal with someone who has a lot of scabs, then cut out a large quantity of the paper according to how soft the paper is; then make an incision all along the sputum-filled area above the two lines that you have marked, and start from the large sore up to the small one; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs on the thickened spot like a root; then insert the needle into one of the corners of the skin, then scrape out all the scabs; then sew together the two lips with a stitch made by inserting a thread made of fine wool into a needle, and clean up the blood, and dry out the superfluity of threads on both wounds as much as possible. If you don't do this, then don't bother; then leave the stitches and threads alone for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitches with things that are drying and constricting, because the paper will heal along with the wound and its assembly, but the stitches are useless (as the ancients said), and it's a work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	Il semble que vous souhaitiez continuer l'extrait original avec une autre manière de procéder.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then consider those who mount to equal strengths equally according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are unable to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle where there is one thread, and pass it through the figure; and pass another thread near the big wound, and the second thread near the small one, and tie between your hands the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin above what you have signed, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound with a suture, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointment.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and any time that the hair of the paper is converted: it suits that you use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and in the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of wounds is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole inside according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two fine threads also long as the width of the paper and the space between them is; and consider the two ends of two parts where you hold the strings; then assemble one and the other finely on top of what rises from the paper of oil, and separate the two stitches from the two parts formwise; and let it be for some days, and the skin that has been separated will die, turn black, and fall off, until it peels itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes a long time, you can try to apply more force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound has been closed, and if there is a raise on the paper, and the hair will no longer stick; and that's the shape of the two stitches that you'll make according to this figure, and with this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The stitches are made as follows: you take a fine needle and insert one thread of silk into it, then tie the ends together finely, making sure the length of the threads is about a hand's width. Then, in the same way, you order another thin thread of silk and tie the end of the thread; then place the patient's head on your healthy skin. And let it be in the sun so that the stitches are revealed, because this is a subtle and fine stitch. Then insert the needle into all the flesh at the root of the hair next to the wound, and make it pierce through the paper quickly as you pull it out from the natural hair. Then pull out the hair until it reaches up to the length of the stitches in the paper along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the flesh is torn and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull out the stitches from underneath to all the thread that you have ordered, until the stitches come out through the small hole above and you can see them with your eye. Then you will pull out the stitches and the thread, close the eye, and let it be closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and grows back the flesh. And if the hairs are small, you will accompany one long hair from the natural eyebrows, and raise it along with that which you have left, until it is elongated and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the purging of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or the purging comes into the eye, there are two ways it happens: one natural and the other unnatural. And it occurs suddenly from a wound, cut, or cauterization, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of treating it is that you split the seam, and separate the edges of it, and put in linen tents, and tie them so that they are healed; and it is not necessary to use in its treatment things that dry up and constrict. For if you do this, the disease will return worse than the first one; but I work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or althea and linseed oil cooked together, and ointments made from distilled aquilon in some oil, and I wrap a tent around it and treat them with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you keep watch so it does not heal in its former shape; and these treatments that we have said are nothing other than precautions against this disease from returning in its former shape.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh (or tissue) that comes into the eye.
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is beneath which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and tear and fire cautery and similar things; and the way of working in it so is that you take an awl, with which it has one double thread, and thrust it into the flesh, and make it pierce as far to the left arm vein as to the right, so that the thread comes out in two holes of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above on all the awl, and the handle at one space large.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper comes back according to what is needed, it's good; if not, take one rasp and put it in the incision, and turn the paper, and make two incisions or cuttings inside the paper; and let the holes of the two cuts be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make a shape so that when they are assembled, the figure will be like the figure of a letter which has the name "j.griesche"; then remove the flesh, as much as the edges are worn out from under the paper; then join together the two separate parts, and sew with one thread of linen; then apply the treatment of the said soft medicines, and dressings, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	It seems like this text is describing a medieval medical treatment, likely from the 12th or 13th century. Here's my attempt to translate and interpret it:
dou soudement de la papiere	the suddenness of paper (or possibly "the speed" or "the swiftness") is unclear, as "papiere" could also mean paper or parchment, but here it may have a more figurative sense)
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suddenness occurs in the same manner as paper is soaked with oil, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and hold it at tongs, just until you copy what is written in subtle ink that is neither too thick nor too fine, so that the patient cannot bear ink that is too thick to stain the eye; and your incision, from which you scrape this assembly, should be light so that the paper returns to its natural form; and thus heal the entire assembly, and make the eye clear of bitter salt, and wash it with sweet water, and eyepatch; then place a linen cloth between the paper and the eye, and put moist wool on the eye in abundance of egg whites; and after the third day, use the collyrium and things that soothe until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	The infection of the eye.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil. de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	It seems like we've transitioned from a medical context to a historical/linguistic one.

et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	and when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, you put oil of sela or broth where you distill red wine and seeming corrosive medicines on it, with a cloth soaked in egg white, so that it may be secure from hot aposteme; and if there remains nothing, and the sense of heat does not rise, and you doubt hot aposteme, then leave the eye and cure the aposteme with soothing things for hot aposteme; then come back to your work until it is cured, and thus do what flesh has been joined in the eye by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige. des voines des eulz	Je pense que nous sommes revenus à la partie du texte qui parle spécifiquement des veines des yeux.
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	There are red veins that cover the eye, and prevent the vision from working properly and weaken the eye forever. It is necessary therefore for you to first see if there is a problem with the eye itself, apart from the vein; then treat the eye in this way: instruct the patient to put his head on your shoulder, then suspend those veins as far out as possible according to your skill, and make the needles sharp double, following this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two needles by degrees in one course according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then take the needles and gently force them into those veins, and check the bleeding every hour again until you see those external veins in the eye being removed; and be careful not to prick the oil with the sharp ends of the needles, and do this operation at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you don't miss those veins; and when you have done this, distill green and red vermillion into the eye to corrupt what remains in the vein.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are unable to remove all the blood in that one hour, make a poultice on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and let it stay for several days until the pains have been alleviated and you are assured that an abscess has not formed, then resume doing this in the manner described above until it is healed. de la fistule de l’oil	It seems I was able to decipher some ancient medical text for you. The text appears to be describing a medical procedure for treating a condition known as "fistule de l'oil" or "eye fistula", which is a abnormal connection between the eye and another structure, such as a vein.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The surgeons call them "arissati" fistules: when you treat it with a cautery and burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then it is necessary to cut into the abscess above where it should be dead, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered and you see the corruption and blackness, then reshape it with all the instrument by which this form was created; and it is called an "aspre chief", and should be made of iron into a shape resembling a .i. (one) sharp point, and should be sharpened like a chisel so that it resembles the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it on the place of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is reduced; and do this several times, then restore the place with medicinal cauterizers.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the place is healed, and flesh is growing, and the body of the fistula is healed, and remains so for 40 days, and it does not recur or become inflamed, and no bad accident happens, then you know that it is healed; if not, there is only one other remedy to bring the fistula back to its original place according to this form: and that is to uncover the bone a second time with iron and burning medicine, and when it is uncovered, take .i. (one) forceps according to this form, and the iron beaks should have three angles, and the handle should be thinned down to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone next to the ulcer, and move your hand away from the eye a little bit, then turn the forceps all the way until it penetrates the bone and the patient feels the instrument if they hold their hand over their navel; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows back and hardens the place, then let the matter drain into the navel; it is a much lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	From the pus of the eye.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye opens wide and there is no disturbance or reduction in sight, it's time to let the patient see again. Then dress the wound with a poultice made from acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla, and then bandage the eye over with cloths and drapery. The manner of tying the drapery is this: take soft cloth and double each piece four times, and then place one on top of the other as needed for the size of the wound. Then tie it down with a sturdy bandage, and repeat the application of the poultice and drapery and the ventouses to suck out any remaining pus without causing further harm.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	A fall from a high place.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the tear comes in the conjunctival sac, it opens, and comes forth with threads like a drop of resin, and it is terrible to see; then if you close it, the stitches are such that you would put an awl into the root of the lower part, as far as up to the upper one, then put another awl where there is a double thread in the eye of the tear; and make it pierce, and leave the first awl according to its position; then close the hole of the double thread and tie a part of the conjunctiva around, and tighten it well, then extract the awl and put on the oily linseed oil soaked in egg white; and let it stay until the thread sticks with the conjunctiva, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and at any time the wound is tightened by the conjunctiva each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye seems to have a great appearance, then make it pierce with a very fine awl that comes into the depth of the eye, and repair the moistened albugo and descend the eye, and enter inside quickly; then extract it until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Il semble que vous me donnez des extraits d'un texte ancien qui décrit des traitements pour les maladies oculaires.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This illness which is called "alcunnati" is not far from what is assembled in the eye, resembling a thread descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is such that you make the patient sit on one prepared and straight chair, then take hold of the head between your hands of two parts, and pull so much until you see the thread come up to your eyes; then stop and do not descend and be extinguished the light, and see the patient's things as he usually does it; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and when the descending of the thread is not prepared as we have said, make the patient sit between your hands, then take the fine spatula and do on the corneal veil one drop by the continuation of the conjunctive with the corneal veil and the crown, so much until the thread comes out; and when it has come out, distill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or boiling onion or fenugreek is boiled and mixed with honey, then be cured with another cure until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	This text appears to be a medical term or description from an older language, likely Old French. Here's my attempt to translate it into English:
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have the likenesses of the eyes in division, and what is necessary for piercing; do this in work according to health. You must have the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and the good eye steady and held very tight; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the good eye is on the left, or in your right hand if the good eye is on the right; then take with your right hand, if the good eye is on the left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or with your left hand, if the good eye is on the right; then place the point of the instrument near the crown through the thickness of a grain in that paper of the eye to the part less minor tear, then thrust the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces into the paper of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the breadth which is from the pupil to the end of the black part; and that is the crown of the eye; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the corneal tissue, and then place the instrument just to the place where the eye is, then press downwards under a way after another. If the eye is now empty, the patient will see before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	C'est le reste de la procédure pour soigner l'œil.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", about which I am going to tell you.
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctiva carefully, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put almagda in, as we have said; and at the end of the work, prepare for the patient a comfortable bed, in which he will sleep on his back in a dark place; and take care to keep him still, and give him light food, and do not let him move his head or turn to the right or left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then release it in that same dark house, examine his sight, make him look at some things, and then remove the bandage until the seventh day; and you must not do this work now in the cure or after the incision, but rather delay it, because the eye will rise quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If a tumor or swelling appears, then remove the bandage from the eye before the seventh day, and turn it towards what alleviates the swelling; and when it is calmed down, then release the eyelid and put on its face a patch, i.e. an ointment, to cover for some days, and let it be in that dark house. And then go out of the house step by step, and change into their clothes; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the region of Yrach (a medieval name for Iraq or Persia), and he said that in his peaceful land, they used to perform almagda incision, by which they could cure the eye, but I have never seen anyone do this in our land, nor did I ever read about it in old books; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the forms of the shapes of almagda, because he who does not know them will see them; and they are made of pure silver.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads should be shaped in the same subtlety, and the back end should have three sharp corners.
de la char sor le neis	This appears to be a fragment of text that doesn't form a complete sentence or idea. "De la char" could mean "from the flesh", and "sur le neis" could mean "on the skin" or something similar, but it's unclear without more context what this line is referring to.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	There are times when various kinds of flesh or skin growths appear on the body, some of which resemble scorpions in shape. And if there is such a one, it may have a flesh-colored spot on it, and also have a foul-smelling flesh-colored sore nearby. In this case, then, take the patient and sit them down facing the sun; open their nostrils, and pour a liquid medicine into those growths, and drive them out from the inside. Then cut out what you can hold onto with the thin sharp instrument on one side, until you know that the growth is entirely gone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there remains anything that cannot be cured, then treat with all kinds of subtle instruments lightly, if nothing remains; and if it swells up or becomes an abscess, then apply the poultice as is necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize so long as the blood is stopped and all the pus is removed, then throw out vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the poultice works and the swelling comes just up to the palace of the nose, know that he is healed; and if the poultice does not penetrate as it should, know that there is pus in the bone above, for the instruments do not come to cut: then you must insert one thread of linen, a little thick, and wrapped with your hands so that each node has about one inch or less; and put the patient's head on the thread in his navel as much as power allows, and tie it so that it comes out through the nose into the mouth; and many times do thus the children at school, and it is a light thing for him who wants to do it; then take the end that comes out through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other as they are on the thread. Do this so long as you know that the nodes have corrupted all the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe the blood, and wet the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back on the navel just as before; do this three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of flesh; and then put on the navel a gauze for some days until he is healed, and if he needs dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, by which one distills oils and medicines into the navel:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or lead, resembling an open lamp, like a candle, and guide them likewise; and if you see that you must make a closed candle, and the instruments are full to purify the head; and have one handle on the head to hold it when one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Il semble que vous avez mentionné une partie du texte qui n'est pas directement liée à la traduction précédente.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises in the head of one who has suffered from it; it grows and becomes large eventually to the point where it is visible to look at; and therefore you must cut out the diseased part at the beginning, and burn the bone entirely, then apply the cautery or hot medicine on top of it; and if you delay cutting it out until it is large, take note whether it has become hard, dark in color, lacking sense: do not touch it with iron because that's a malignant abscess, for when you cut into it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of pure appearance, not dark in color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, the patient feels empty and free from pain, and cures quickly of things constricting and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the diseased part is cut out and cauterized
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is known that when a sore comes to the cartilage of the ear, it benefits little, or rather harms some people. It therefore happens sometimes that one looks and sees if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then sews up the two lips with a suture, and cures until they are healed; and if the lips are already separated from each other in parts, it is necessary to scrape out all the parts of their flesh until they heal, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and bind them tight, and sprinkle on top powder of dragon's blood and powdered incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of hot or another binding plaster, and let it alone until it comes off by itself, then cure with ointment until they are healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of the suture is that you assemble the parts together with:
des apostemes des levres	swellings of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Sometimes at home swellings appear inside the lips which are hard, resembling grains of millet, small and large; then you must turn the lips back and split each one with a knife and take it to the pincers and cut into each part; then apply vinegar to the place after the incision, so that the swelling is dulled; and then let it dry out and cure the place with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the gum flesh
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often on the gums a tumor-like flesh appears, which the old call "albulus"; it is necessary that you hold it with pincers and cut at its root and let blood or pus come out; then apply vinegar to the place or other drying and desiccative powders; and if that flesh comes back after the incision and often happens, then cut it again and cauterize it: if it does not come back after cauterizing, those are the forms of tumors for cutting.
des sordens	of the ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the molars, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black and greenish and wormy, until corruption comes to the gum, and it smells bad; then you need to have the patient sit in your hands, and his chin be on your saint (knee?), and remove the molars or scabs that show, as long as there's nothing left; and similarly do with the blackness, greenishness, yellowness, and other spots, until they are clean; and if you take out what was at the first cause, it's good; but if not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have everything removed; and know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because the scrapers that are used to remove molars outside the teeth have different forms than those used to remove them between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you ready.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It's necessary when you cure a tooth from its pain that you don't rush to draw it out as soon as you can, because it shouldn't be done; for it's a very high substance, just so there should be no excuse for drawing it. (This text is talking about the importance of not removing a tooth too quickly or prematurely, likely in a dental procedure)
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	So when the patient is being constrained to have it drawn out, you need to be certain that it's the rotten tooth. Many times the pain deceives the patient and they think it's a healthy tooth, and they make them pull the good tooth; and yet the pain doesn't depart for this reason, until the bad tooth is pulled, because we've already wanted to do this with these saints (healthy people). And when you're well certain that it's the rotten tooth, then you need to scrape around the tooth on all sides, making a deep cut in order to protect the gum from every part; then move the tool to your hands or thin pincers at the first point and point, until they are well closed, then tighten the pincers; and have the patient's chin be on your knee between your knees, and hold it well so that it doesn't move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, if it doesn't come out easily, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side lightly, and then move it as you did initially. And if the tooth is pierced or broken, you need to fill it with thread, where the holes are; and if you're using fine pincers, make sure not to break it when extracting it; and it's also necessary to work carefully around the gum in order to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And do well in warning that you don't break it, and leave a part of it, and return to the patient with greater pain from the root than the first. And be aware that you don't do thus as foolish doctors do, who by their haste and boldness break some time the chariot, and do not bring what we have told; but sometimes bring great disease through the roots that remain, or through the chariot they break, as often happens to us; and when the tooth is loose, wash the place with wine or vinegar and gall; and if there is bleeding from it which often happens, apply the place with vitriol powder; and if this does not help, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, by which one should extract the tooth first, should be long with pointed tips and thick handles, so that they do not double when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should have thick handles so that they do not bend when pulled, and should be well-made iron, and should have teeth to hold firmly.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains at the pull, it is necessary that you put on the place moist cotton in butter, i.e. one or two days, until the place is softened, then insert the pincers called "algefri", by which the tooth seems to be the beak of a hawk; and they should be inside made as a file and this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pincers, it is necessary that you uncover the whole char around the root, and then put the instrument called "althali", i.e. a file, which has this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps through it, it's good; if not, use all the instruments, by which these shapes come next:

et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other bandages which are before in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which seems great pincers, whose shape is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is except that it cannot break; and know that many instruments of dens are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise master skilled finds by himself his instrument, according to the works and the disease it shows him, for there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach an instrument because of the diversity of them and such that it does not break a bone or the other bones, or it is possible, if he looks for the instruments which it needs, as I have told you, and helps from gestures, of what this shape is.
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be big and well holding to hold the bone so it does not slip away but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place of medicines corresponding to those, and if there is in the bone putrefaction, and it is small, then reap all this instrument.

Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and short in your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears to be able to be filed, take the file with this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also done with the lime of which we make needles; and in sharpening the point of a tooth one should do so little by little over many days, so that it does not move until it becomes sharp; then polish at the end with no rasp at all, and if the teeth are too pointed and they hurt the tongue, you must whet the roughness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth falls out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front tooth falls out, either by being knocked out or falling out, and the patient cannot press on what they eat without it hurting, and you have treated them with restricting medicines, but that doesn't work; then they need to be restrained with a thread of gold, because threads of silver become green and rotten, but gold does not change; and the middle thread should neither be too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see the tooth loose, take the thread and tie it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the ends between the loose teeth, as many as there are, until you have securely tied them up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover the covering up to the part where you started, and carefully and subtly strain your hand, so that they do not move; and make sure your thread is at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then take the ends of the thread in a pair of pliers, and assemble them, and point them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it tied tightly as long as it can remain, and if it loosens, or the threads break, then tighten with another thread; if it remains and serves in this way for all its time, and that is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, if you put it back in place, fresh and fresh, just as we have said; and do not interfere with it unless one is wise and patient, and sometimes one makes a form of an ivory tooth, and puts it in the place where the defect is, and tightens it as we have said, and it remains and serves in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Il semble que cette phrase soit une instruction pour faire une manipulation sur le fil d'or qui relie les deux dens.

des apostemes de la gorge	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! Les apostèmes de la gorge sont des ulcères ou des tumeurs qui se forment dans la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron either, also for the sake of bloodletting; but leave it until it dies, and then you will part it, or it would break on its own; and if it is pale in color, and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to cut, but first look to see if the abscess has cooled down and is appeased. Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and your hands be steady, and the work open the mouth and take hold of the servant between his hands, and press the tongue under the entire instrument, because that is its shape; and it should be thin like a silver or copper knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against this entire instrument, and you will see the abscess, then take the needle and stick it in the almond, and the thread should be above as much as your thumb; and remove any threads that are attached to the skin, then cut the abscess at the instrument, because of its shape, which resembles a claw; and though the tip is curved, one end to the other, and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	Je crois que je vois où ça va !
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament. Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij.
