And I treated a woman with a tumor that had grown inside her throat, to be specific a small swelling of the uvula; and it had almost completely closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the airway which was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had stayed like that for one or two days. And the tumor was so swollen that I had to make two incisions with my needle through the two openings of the mouth. I acted quickly, then stuck the needle into one part of it, then extracted a large portion of mucus; then made another incision in the other opening of the mouth and extracted more mucus from it, and closed up her mouth and pressed down on her tongue; after that I stuck the needle into this tumor, and cut off a part of it, and only a little bit of blood came out; and thus was the airway opened up for the woman, and she started drinking water and then wine again, and did not stop cutting away at that tumor for a long time; and the tumor kept growing again, and filled up the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left those parts alone, and only knew what God could do with them after me.
de l’uve	Vous semblez avoir lu ce que j'avais traduit, mais vous voulez peut-être juste faire référence à "l'uvée", qui est la partie du pharynx où se trouve le sillon uvulaire (ou uvule), où se produit le son de la "r" et d'autres consonnes. C'est souvent au centre de cette zone que les tumeurs ou les apostèmes pouvaient se former, comme décrit dans le texte original.

de la sansue de la gorge	The passage appears to be a medieval medical text, possibly from the 14th or 15th century, written in French. It describes a procedure for treating a throat abscess or infection.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	When the medicine of bloodletting is often prescribed as I have said in the division, by the treatment of medicines; and when it does not profit at all, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun, and after you press the tongue with the instrument that I told you. And if you see blood, take away all little by little or with delicate tweezers that are worth for this purpose. And if it does not help, take a long string and put it in the throat of the patient, then push the head of the string with a hot iron and do this often. And if the patient suffers from water every day, then take a full glass of cold water and open the mouth, and pour it out without swallowing, and move it to his hand often; and as soon as the blood tastes the water, it will flow.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not flow as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida at the instrument that I told you in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, for it will come out soon. The manner of fumigation is to take a pot in which there are glowing coals and let the cover be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that hole put the end of the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the string in his mouth and closes it, so that the smoke does not come out but comes up to the blood; and the blood will now flow, and if it does not flow, start the fumigation again many times; and let the patient be thirsty, eat salty foods and others, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to come out through this management.

li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many similarities of abscesses are described in the remembrance that comes later in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which one is itself similar, and due to its moistness. And the second manner is for those places where it is at the body. For the abscess of the head is different from that of the foundation, and the abscess of a fleshy place is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And there are abscesses that should not be punctured until the swelling is dead according to its completion; and there are those that require puncturing when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that come near joints. For when an abscess comes near a joint, and one leaves it until it is purulent around it, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may become corrupted, thereby causing contraction in that member.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary that you know the order of the perforation of the abscess which is known according to its completion, and this is when the pain has been alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the settling down and becoming calm of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation situate as dependent on the place of the abscess, and where it opens most easily; and the perforation should be made long into the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those places where they swell, according to the place of that member. And when abscesses are in fatty places, it is worth noting that you should leave the perforation until it has been confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce them before this, the body will become engorged with venom and be filled with much foulness; and perhaps the lips and deeper parts of it will harden. And when any abscesses are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs. And it is necessary that you make small perforations in small abscesses, small holes; and large perforations in large abscesses, and many fissures according to the resemblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to sew up the core, and cover; when it has become as hard as a flagstone, and is worn out, you should do as one does for boils: and if there are such that are split into three angles, and if there are such that one covers like the stem of myrtle, like abscesses of the groin; and if there are such where one makes a round cut, and other cuts and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who do not have a head, like superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them thoroughly. And if the abscess is large and has accumulated much pus, when you pierce it, do not pull out all the pus at once, but only part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then remove any remaining thing from it; do this several times in turns, as long as the pus comes out entirely. Likewise if the patient is weak or a woman in childbirth, or small children, or old men who are decrepit. For the expectation (of life) can suddenly jump with the exit of the pus, and perhaps the patient will die, and you won't be aware of it. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, squeeze the wound, and look if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it's a smooth incision, sew up with threads of linen or old cotton; and if it's a large abscess, and there are many holes, it is necessary that you stuff each one with a thread so that they come together; and if you have sewn up in the abscess a part of the skin, and you have covered it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or with rags of linen soaked in water, and tie it until the third day; then take it out, and cure it with ointment as long as it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs from the wound, mix cold water and vinegar, and wet a cloth with it, and put it on the bleeding wound several times. And if the bleeding from the wound persists, add governance and care, and the powders that I have said to be used in this book, and if it's during the summer, and the skin or the abscess is very sensitive, it is necessary that you put wet cloths and blankets on it with wine and hot oil; and if it's during the winter, and the skin is fleshy, it is necessary that you put wet cloths and blankets on it with water and cold oil, or with vinegar and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then untie the abscess and squeeze and cure it as it should be, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	It is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should go before treating abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	of little boils that come to the head in small pustules, and are signs of what is in the boil, just like the threads from a silkworm's cocoon, and there are many similarities. There are some that are fat and moist, just like pus; and those that are hard and stony when cut into them, and it can't be doubted that the abscess made them contrary. The procedure for cutting is to try with all sorts of instruments called "entromissoires", from which their shape comes next, whatever they contain. If it contains moisture, you do it above the length. And when the moisture is emptied, you soak up nothing except the peel that contained that moisture, because it returns again if you leave anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it's present; if not, in water and oil, and dress the wound, and leave it just until the next day; and those who are left overnight will be cured. And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it doesn't stay overnight; then heal the wound with ointment according to what is suitable, until it's sound. And if the pustules hold one night of fatness, cut them according to this form, from above; and I throw out my threads, and scrape off all around, and put all your cure in a poultice where it lies; and if the abscess makes you contrary, do what I told you afterwards. And similarly with the pustule if it is stony, and hard to cut into, and to heal as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	The procedure for cutting the abscess that is stony and moist is lighter, because they are full of blood. And some of these abscesses, on the head or where there is no moisture, and this was one abscess I cut on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a hard stone, rough and white, and couldn't be broken; and if you had done any surgery on it, you would have made a wound as from a rock. On other abscesses that come to the head, such as those that come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the bottom, so that the pus can drain out; and they should be cured as is suitable.
des scrophules	from swellings
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	These swellings often occur in the neck and under the arms and in the groin, and sometimes they come in other places on the body, and are soft, and are joined one to another. And each swelling is properly contained within its own skin, just as the boil and the swelling of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these swellings are many. There are some such that contain moisture, and there are some malicious ones that will not obey the law of health. Therefore, when you see one with a good disposition to touch, and it is similar in color to the body, and is soft on each side and is not hardened under the skin of the neck or at the artery or at the duct, and is not deep; then you should cover it up, and scrape off all around it, and sew up the two lips of the skin with stitches if necessary, as we have said about swelling of the head; and pull out the pus little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not leave any part that should not be left.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it doesn't stop bleeding, then apply vitriol or any powder that stops blood and constricts the wound, and leave it like that until the swelling is calmed down and the wound is softened and begins to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work and finish it; then check if there are any small swellings left behind, and cut them out and clean them.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut out the whole scrophule, it is necessary that you close together the two lips of the wound, and sew them up now, since there remains no superfluity because of the greatness of the scrophule. It is necessary that you understand to cut out the root of it, and draw out pus, and sew it as we have said. Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce at the place where it most hurts; and pierce just like the one mentioned before, in a dependent manner, then insert tenths with ointment and similar things, so that what remains of the corruption corrupts them; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply ointment with grease, until it be healed.
de squinance	Swelling.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and talked about the surgery of the throat; but I never saw in our land anyone who did it, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have swelling, it is necessary that the incision in the throat which is called "epiglottis" be cut out; and this should not be helped by those [doctors], because all the veins and the pus of the sick person are in those who have suppurative fever in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both nostrils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pus, it is necessary to cut out the epiglottis to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut out the epiglottis, we must cut it under three or four circles, or a small incision across, between the two circles, or by the size of the incision of the syphac, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and those who are suitable for the section of the epiglottis do not have flesh and the blood vessels are long in length.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches out the skin of the throat to its entire length, then cuts through the skin as far as the channel; and drains the blood vessels from bleeding, if you see any, and then cut out the syphac, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein in the channel which bursts forth through the place that is broken, and by the defect of the voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and let the wound be left open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed by which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the skin and sew them all alone except for the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	I myself say that we do not make this procedure until the throat is completely swollen and the patient has been judged to be at death's door, and the fault lies in the haemorrhage.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then we cut out the epiglottis because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and because of this the ancient ones commanded to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease had passed, and it passes in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they instructed to sew up the wound and treat it until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young woman took, i.e., a dagger, and thrust it into her throat, and cut off part of the veins of her privates.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to go cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had come out of it, and I saw clearly that she hadn't cut deeply enough nor had the artery been cut, and the vein was issuing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, sewed up the wound, and treated her until she was healed.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and nothing happened to the young woman except that she became hoarse in her voice, and returned afterwards to her usual state.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	so I say that in sewing up the epiglottis one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This hernia is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a great swelling in colour like jet, and it is very common among women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; or the natural kind has no defect.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental kind is in two ways: one of which resembles a fatty nodule, and the other manner resembling an abscess that comes from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it does not seem fitting to operate unless the tumor is small, and the proof and search of the entire interior.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it to be just like a small fatty nodule, and it cannot be cut in any way, then you should cut it, as one cuts the lymph nodes, and treat its entire head, if there is no swelling.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search very well all around, and cure it just as is fitting, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of the lymph nodes
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many kinds of lymph nodes, and I will say all their similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary for me to tell all the difference which is between them and us.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever holding, as long as the boiling has passed, and the purtification is completed; then the fever and heat rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With us, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and the suppurating fluid, that is its own sack, and is according to the color of the body, and also begins like a scab, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are in two ways, thick or moist, and very much of color are such as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of us, that you inquire and examine first with all the instrument which is called "intromissor", according to what its form will come or chapter which comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring the apostemes of us is that you take or the most moist part that you find in the aposteme, and turn your two pots and pot, so long as you know that the instrument has pierced deep enough, then it will be according to the size of the aposteme.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then pull out the intromissor and take care that nothing spills over.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If it is a moist core, cut it, whatever its color may be, do with it as I said about the other apostemes.
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the intromissor there comes no moisture, know that it is thick, then do with it as a cross, and take it to the lancets, and lightly scrape each part and wrap in a cloth where it lies so that you may draw out the pus safely with the instrument.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot drain it safely, then drain it in pieces, as long as there remains nothing.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if there remains anything, it will return to the navel many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if there remains a small amount and the navel bothers you, then fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, bind up the wound tightly, and put on soothing things to calm the hot aposteme, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the navel is large, then cut the two edges of the wound, and treat it with those things that prevent foul flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the pus boils against you or another complication occurs and you are in a hurry, then use vinegar to soak the area, and let it be for two or three days, until the wound purifies, and calm the ebullition of blood; then come back to cover what is left from the navel.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of intromissor instruments, and they are of three kinds: great, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb", and there are three types of them: great, medium, and small, to encircle the apostemes of fistules.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles with which one sews sutures, and they are of citrine iron, or iron, or silver, and most valuable are those that are yellow, and are more proven to be black lead in encircling the folds of a fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and they are of three kinds: great, medium, and small, according to the size of the diameter of the fistulae.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The forms of lancets are many and varied, as you can see here: great, medium, and small; and there are lancets that have two handles in three manners also.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are lancets that have three handles, and they are also in three manners; and there are lancets that have two handles, and lancets with a single handle only, and they come in three manners; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these lancets are cutting, and there are such that do not cut at all deeply from one side, with which we scrape the nerves, so that one does not cut through the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and among these intromissors are the alemelles, which are made to return in fingers, so that the patient does not feel them at the opening of the apostemes.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they come in three manners: great, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one does not use them at all in hard places, such as joints, and arms, and shoulders, and the like areas.
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and one never makes another small instrument, resembling scissor-like forceps, according to this shape, with which one stops blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one places it nowhere in the place where veins and arteries suture, and they are never sewn according to this great shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never do the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much that they seem like the breasts of a woman.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them must cut out according to this shape of the line b up to 7:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape out the fat, and fill the wound with medicine preventing foul flesh, then sew together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the breast sags downwards and is droopy because of its size just like in women, then they make it in two folds upwards with two similar incisions.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one edge is attached to the other at the end of both, so that the longer line contains the shorter one according to this shape, from line b up to line g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape out the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitches and powders, and everything that is necessary for the treatment, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, it is necessary that you fill the wound with moist cotton in caustic oil.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and let it be until it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of the abscesses in the buttocks.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are kinds of hard scrofulas with or without tubercles, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture then need to be cut open according to this shape, from line b up to line g:.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole abscess that is in the abscess has been emptied, one fills the wound with fresh cotton and leaves it until the next day, then removes all the cotton and treats it with suitable ointment as needed until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to a scrofula, one cuts it in the same way we have said for cutting scrofulas, and if the wound turns into an abscess again, one applies cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it is sewn up, then many abscesses come, and just as well it has swollen veins and an abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows how to recognize it when it is due to the artery, then the abscesses are long and deep.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel one swelling; and when it is due to the vein, then there are several swellings appearing on the surface.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is folly to cut this abscess, and even more so when it is under the buttocks and arms and neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one should flee from the iron treatment, and so should the person who is in charge, and in that which is due to swelling of an artery, they should make a cut above the skin long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then operate on the wound with lancets, and carefully separate the artery from the tissue, until it is fully exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle under the artery, and make it pierce through to the other side, and tie off the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have shown you in extracting the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then sew up the place between the two threads with an intromissor needle until the blood that was inside comes out, and thus loosen the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then apply the treatment that prevents a clot from forming, until the thread dries.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with suitable ointment as needed, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to a cut on the vein, it is necessary that you dye with your hand what you can extract from the abscess into all the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the place that you have in your hand, and make it pierce through, and there will be a double thread, so that you can pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie off the abscess, just like I told you, by tying one of the two ends of the thread to the other two holes of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you doubt that the thread will not come out strong enough, then insert another needle into all of one thread under all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tie off the threads in four places.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut open the abscess until the excess comes out, then cut off the excess skin and leave what is tied.
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply a damp cloth soaked in vinegar and oil on top of it, then apply treatments of poultices and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses in the groin area.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just like abscesses that come in the artery and vein, there are abscesses in the groin area when they are heated, or from excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this happens more often in the joints and arms and in all places where there are joints, and it is a serious abscess, and its color seems like the color of flesh, and it feels in various positions with pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when one extracts it properly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	and it can spread in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, up or down, and the one that is in joints should not be cut with iron: perhaps there would be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and the one that is in the head or on the forehead, make a cut on the scalp.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then tie it with pincers and cut it at its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, then scrape it with a lancet, and remove the dead tissue, then sew up the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Of swollen and hanging cheeks.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	It sometimes occurs in the stomach and not elsewhere the throat, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and has fine roots and a large swelling; and there are small and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen one man who had two growths in his stomach that were more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, with a small root, and were cut open and dripping with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I cut them open and found that one weighed 28 ounces and the other 7 pounds, and in the incision I saw that the patient's body was moist, and the color of the tissue was white and moist with a subtle root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	I cut them open on the scalp with a large incision, and had the cautery at the fire ready. For when cutting comes, there are often too great bleeding of blood, and if the blood spills over, you should then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient trembling and fearful of the incision with iron, then take a well-made thread of silk and tie the wound as we have said, and let it be for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then let it heal, and do not cease to tighten the thread of silk until it cuts through the wound and you feel that the work is done; and if the roots are thick, be afraid even more so when cutting with the belly, but you can well cut half.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then cauterize it so that it does not recur, then treat the wound and be careful that you do not cut the throat which has a foul color and poor sense and milky reek.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an enchanted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of chancre later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the swelling has hardened.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the swelling comes from a cauterization of a wound or an incision of a syphac, and is on the stomach and in one of the swellings, just as it happens in other cuts, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries, according to what has been said before, or from windiness.
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the rupture of the syphac and from the discharge of pus, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens with a various outlet.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the discharge of the intestine, then it is more varied. And when you press it with your fingers, it becomes tense, and then returns to its normal state, and perhaps it is swollen, and greatly increases in size at the entrance of the anus and after hard work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is from moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand, without constraint. And if it is from blood, then the abscess opens in great quantity, and is filled according to its size.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is from windiness, then it is soft to the touch, and the works are such that you can see if the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of a vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Then you should leave the treatment. For there is doubt and fear, just as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, then it is necessary that you command the patient to strain his stool and be straightened out completely, then sign them all around the swelling.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to lie down on his back between your hands.
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	then go around the place that you have signed all around the scalp.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then separate the top of the abscess to the middle with a large lancet.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk tightly, and make the ends of the thread equal.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then operate on the middle of the abscess that is stretched out above the thread, and insert your index finger and feel the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught on the thread, then release it, and push the intestine back into the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, then take it with the lancet, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein is in your way, then go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and tie the two strong threads, and insert the two needles around what you have done, piercing through it.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then tie the abscess in four places above the needles, and if it seems good, remove the needles, and let the place be until it heals, and the dead flesh will fall off by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or you can cut it when it has softened and fallen off, then treat it with what is necessary, and have the abscess come out as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place with what is necessary, and close the wound.
dou chancre	Of a chancre (syphilis).
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division about the symptoms of chancre and how to work with medicines, and how to avoid iron treatment. And we say that chancre begins in the groin area and requires great caution in its treatment. The ancient ones said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be scraped out, such as on the breasts, or in the thighs, or in similar places, it should all be removed at the beginning. And when it is large and old, then you must not approach it, because I have never seen anyone cured of it; nor has anyone ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the procedure, when it is in a place where it can be scraped out, as we have said, is to purge the patient with black bile at least once. Then make them drink something that will help cleanse their system, if they are manifestly full. Then prepare the patient for the operation by making a good place to do the work. Then throw away your lancets or chancre, and let it drain out of all places without leaving anything behind. Let the blood dry up completely, and test the place with your hand or some other object. If the bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein makes you afraid, then cauterize it until the bleeding is stopped. Then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy (edema).
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have said in the division about the symptoms of dropsy and how the assembly of water is formed, and the signs of each symptom, and the treatment that is made by medicine, and that which is cured by iron. This one is called "eclites" and only swells; and you must not touch it with iron in these two symptoms: tympanites and hyposarchia, because they are mortal things. So when you medicate this symptom of dropsy that is called "eclites" with medicines and the treatment does not help, look to see if the patient is weak or has another disease besides dropsy, such as a twist in the intestines and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, because there is doubt. And if you see the patient of strong virtue, and they have only dropsy and are neither too young nor too old, then you should operate thus:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lift the patient up straight with your hands, and have the attendants press the stomach from below, pushing the water to the lowest part of the belly. Then take the scalp lance according to this shape: it should be cut through in two parts at a point, but not so deeply that it can reach the intestine when you insert it, and cannot bleed.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look if the dropsy is extended towards the intestines: if so, it is necessary that you cut into the belly three fingers to the right on top of the navel; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, the incision should be on the left side of the belly three fingers; and if it is due to the spleen, the incision should be on the right, and it must not be that the patient lies over the incision so that the superfluites do not flow towards that weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the skin up to the instrument, and plug it in, and lift your hand to all the spatula between the skin and the syphac as much as is equal to the tip of a finger or slightly more; then pierce the syphac until the spatula comes out, and that is the place of the water, then draw it forth, and put this instrument from which it is shaped: And it looks like a silver thread fine, and it is made of lead or of very light metal, and in the lower part there is one small hole; and on either side there are three holes, and two on another part, and one on another; and the strings are cut so that they resemble a feather, and that is the shape of the incision from which the scribes cut the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	At the top there is the alembic, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it now descends on the instrument; empty then one half or one third of it, because if you empty more than it should be at this hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the arm, or he will faint, or he will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	But empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's virtuous signified, and his pulse; then draw the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now by the key which closes the hole that is on the syphac, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then resume the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering these things, and draw from the water a small quantity.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this every day, and be careful not to leave too much water in him. And if you doubt the patient, and you leave a lot of water, he will die from the fever or hot sand, and by sweating or bath and sun, and turn black as pitch; and he will be cured with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, just as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes children are born without a penis in their scrotum, or the penis is small, or it is not in its proper place. So you should pierce them immediately with one very sharp needle, very thin according to this shape: then put into the penis one very fine piece of cloth, tie and hold it like that for three days or four; and when they want to urinate, take out the cloth, let them urinate, and then replace it; and it may not be necessary at all, because the urine that comes out will keep the opening closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose penis is small, if they have the cloth of linen medicine, as we said, it will enlarge. Those who do not have their penis in its proper place are blind, because none are born with their penis at the head of their scrotum, why can they not urinate unless they lift their scrotum upwards; and cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come up to the foreskin, and this is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way to do this surgery is that the sick person lies on their back most of the time, with the head of the penis and scrotum hanging down like a hen's tail, so that the foreskin can come into place as it should; and be careful to stop the bleeding which comes out many times, and if it happens, stop the bleeding with what stops bleeding blood, and care for the wound until they are healed.

de la circoncision	the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the removal of a continuation like other wounds; however, when we do this work of our own will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the easiest for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention the circumcision of their children, because they did not practice it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greater part of masters and sages who performed circumcision around a candle, with forceps, and all a novacula; it was frightful because there were two threads, and by chance one above remained and the other below stayed.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it is necessary to cauterize, and the pain is doubled, and with the purification which is on the candle, the point of the member is not assured; and with the purification of the wound, by chance the iron slips and runs off the work, and many times they are born in such a way that there is no need for purification and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Regarding the purification which is done with forceps, I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the forceps cut exactly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	Because when you press your hand, it cuts equally both above and below. puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the fist in the purging is thus: the two fists should be clenched and cut, and the fingers should be as long as the palm equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the purging is when the pus inside escapes through the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your fingernail, so that the place makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingers, then hold it with forceps, and then cut.

dou retenement de l’urine	It seems like you're quoting a medieval medical text again!

et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is caused by a stone in the bladder or the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent over their knees; and have their feet on their back, and extend their belly from the upper part of their back, and pull the patient's loin as much as they can; and then force the neck of the bladder to express the stone above, so that the urine is released.

de l’aposteme des coions	This appears to be a heading or title in an old medical text, possibly from Middle English or Old French. The phrase "de l'apostème des coïons" can be translated to "on the apostème of the scrotum" or "treatment for an abscess of the testicles".
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the surgery of this remedy against evil humors, there are several preparations, for which reason it seems to me that it is more valuable to leave it.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you the work and the symptoms of the apostème.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that many abscesses come from within the body, and also from the testicles; and this is because of many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It happens to be due to an acid or bilious superfluity that spreads to the testicles, or from a blow.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and it does not find pain, and it is a grievous abscess.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and it is possible that there are grievous, painful and bloody abscesses, and of a foul color, and which sometimes come from no artery, or from an inflamed vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from no artery, it is known by the disposition of the warm abscess, when you press it to your fist;

de l’aposteme des coions	A book of medieval medical text, specifically on "De Apostema Testiculorum", which translates to "Of the Abscess of the Testicles". The text appears to be written in an old French style and provides a description of how to diagnose and treat abscesses of the testicles.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enveloped by a swelling similar to a boil, with the softening of the testicles.
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	And if the patient moves suddenly when he walks;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment for this disease is just as painful as the previous one.
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	and we will tell you all about it anyway, according to what the old ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	You should have the patient sit on an elevated seat, then place the suspensory of the testicles down to your elbows.
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	to all the veins that are close to the penis, and tie them tightly with threads, and stretch them out properly.
