dou chastrement	The correction of a bruise.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The correction of a bruise is known in our law, and for that reason it would please me not to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary for two purposes: one is that the surgeon knows how to respond when asked, and know how to cure it; and the other, because we often need to correct some animals to help us, such as donkeys, sheep, goats, and other animals. I say then that corrections are made in two ways: by attraction or by tearing apart.
des hermofrodites	those with two sexes
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	They are hermaphrodites in two ways like men: one way is if between the two testicles it opens as much as the figure of a woman's nature, or if there is hair and sometimes urine. And the other manner is in women, who have on the navel as much as a penis and two testicles. And the cure for man and woman is that you bind the swollen parts together, and heal them like other wounds; in the second manner, men whose urine shoots through the skin of the testicles have no cure.
de la tentigene	of the hydra-like birthmark (tenta means "hydra" or "water-snake")
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The tentigene is a swollen part on the natural place, so ugly to see; and some women have it as big as a hand, and that's the cure. You should dye the excess of the tentigene to your hand or nails, and bind it lightly; and don't go too deep, lest there come bleeding, then cure it with another cure until it is healed; and there is another mark that appears on the mouth of the womb, and you should cover it, and perhaps it will burst forth, and it looks like a cow's shape, and for that reason they called it in ancient times "cow disease". You should bind it, as we said to bind the tentigene, and cure it until it is healed.

des emorroides	from hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that swell without their usual covering, and when hemorrhoids become old they turn into ulcers; and we have said in the division the likenesses of them and the signs, and I will say now those which receive a cure. I say that hemorrhoids and ulcers, when they are deeply embedded in the rectum and cannot be felt, cannot be cured except with a lancet. Those which are at the entrance of the rectum, where one can feel them, are those which can be cured. It is necessary then to place the woman in a cold room, then set the ulcer on fire with tongs, and bind its roots with a cloth; then powder on medicine to stop bleeding, such as aloes and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her into cold water; and if she has bleeding, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and apple peel and galls and similar things, and then take fine flour and mix it with honey and oil, and make one poultice on her back. And if it stops, that is good. If not, make ventouses to the back and shoulders so as to cause pain; then take linen and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of elderberry with old wine, and make it hot. And when the swelling subsides, cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to a sharp head, so it should be covered as I said about ulcers; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Il s'agit d'un passage du texte qui semble traiter des abcès (apostèmes) qui se forment dans le rectum (marris). Voici une traduction et une interprétation plus précises :
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess occur in the groin, such as carbuncle and abscessed pierous and herpes and scrofula and fistules and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I said in the division. It is necessary then that I say in this treatise the hot abscess which occurs in the groin, which is not one of the abscesses that cool; and if you want to know how to work with iron, see if the abscess is sharp at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red as far as you can see. Then do not hasten to pierce, but let it subside until the pain is alleviated; and then have the patient sit on one stool, and have two small stools where he leans forward, and support his back and bring his feet towards the outer side of the leg; and have his thighs spread wide apart, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good cord. Then make an incision on the right side and insert the instrument through which the mouth of the groin comes out, by means of which the abscess will form; and it is necessary that when you see to inserting this instrument, you first insert the drill so that you can know the depth of the groin, so that what enters through the instrument does not penetrate more deeply than it should, and does not harm the patient. And if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the groin with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary to put the nozzle of the instrument above, and tie the instrument. And when the abscess opens up and you make a cut with a soft cloth, you must close the head at the spur-like part; and when the bowel is empty, you must put in the wound moist sponges soaked in rose oil or green olive oil; and place the sponge outside the wound at the bottom of the groin, and place outside the groin and on the poignil a clean damp cloth soaked in water or marshmallows that have been cooked; then cure after two days of ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is healed; and sometimes open up the wound and the abscess with a wet enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lily and aristologe longa that have been cooked; then return to the ointment. Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument by which one smokes the woman for retention of flowers and secondines is this:

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not had the foundation pierced, but rather it has been stopped up with a subtle and fine scab:
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	so it is convenient to the ball that it pierce the scab at its due time, and not the pointed sharp spatula, and bind the surrounding area so that it does not touch.

de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the fundament are nodular, and grow more than those that come from beside the fundament forward, or in the interval of the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if it has one or more fistulas; and when that nodular swelling is old, it works, and makes a moist or whiteish or fine pus.

et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and then you press your thumb or fundament, and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has tortuosity, you insert a thin linen thread or one hair of a horse, so that you feel the thread or the hair with your thumb.

des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids

Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	If it is necessary to sew the wound in this way: take a twisted thread and put it in a needle, and then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pierced from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread alongside the needle.

dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	when the wound of a devil or foundation (i.e., a dislocation)
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often times happens a wound of the devil in the intestines, and through constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine doesn't help it.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If it suits that you reset to the tip of a splint or at your nail the scab above, which does not let it get moist.

dou fremit	from a burn
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Formication is a small appearance of false ants on the body, and it goes deep.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and sometimes it finds the frost, and one feels it just like a burn of burns, and it comes in all the body, and more so in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a quill of goose feather or a strong swan's feather and put that quill on the burn, as long as the circles purplish the burn all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand back over the quill as long as you cover all around the burn, and put it in deep, and drain the burn of its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see it, make a bandage of lead or iron according to this shape, and be subtle underneath and drawn above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that it does not bleed much, and do not press it hard. And if you see it, burn the burn with a hot iron, as before or with a cauterizer.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a catheter
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At any time made one catheter of silver or gold, or melted lead; and at any time made these instruments small and large, as they are furnished.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore which one furnishes in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small catheter and a large one is thus wide, or the abdomen is tied in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has an opening or the abdomen is tied, as you see, and the cheeks are pierced inside; and it has two holes on one side, and one on the other.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the abdomen is or there put medicines in a bladder of beast or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and it has between each hole one inch of spacing, then put in these holes one strong thread of twisted raw linen yarn in ten or twelve turns, and tie the belly as a goat.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicine is inside, then bind with a strong thread in front of the instrument, and catheterize; and that's the shape of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the top of the catheter with oil or egg yolk or something similar, then put it in lightly.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the servants will grasp it with both hands together, until it is all empty, then remove the catheter, and lift up the patient's legs to the bed.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicine wants to come out, then tie it tightly as much as you can; and if he sleeps one whole night, it is a greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catheterize him in a disease of purging the belly, and the medicine rushes to come out, then repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or growth, then make the catheter as delicate as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and that's the form of the delicate catheter above which the skin is stretched.
des plaies	( new topic )
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken of the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will tell you of the cures for hands and medicines, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse in accordance with how they are made, and in accordance with the places or the wounds are made, and why they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things with which wounds are made are by stumbling against a stone, and cutting of sword and knife or spear or fist or arrowhead, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the parts of the body, if a wound falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with the wounds of the head that are simple, because the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, take care if it's from stumbling against a stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt a little of an aposteme (inflammation) being hot: if the face is immediately cleansed and healed from the cephalic liquid itself, even if it comes out in great quantities from the wound, and the skin is healed on the contrary side from the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and give the sick a full measure of wine and heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it doesn't want to heal, make its meat less nourishing, and have it not drink wine nor eat any meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put a poultice on the wound, if an hot aposteme comes, with wet cotton in rose oil only, or in vinegar solution.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot aposteme, put on the wound a powder that I will tell you about shortly.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the burn has healed it, then apply some ointments until it is fully healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar ones, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by suturing, just as I will say about belly wounds, with suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	And if the wound is exposed of bone and flesh, and it's loose and only held by a little bit, then cover it; then treat the wound with medicine, and replace hard meat in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and command the sick person to eat heavy meats, such as roasted chestnuts and wheat bread, also like poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find purpura (a type of skin infection) on the skin and it doesn't affect the bone, then cut out all the purpura, and throw away what's bad, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	And if there is an artery in the wound or vein that won't clot, and it can't be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it cut, then sew it up with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if that doesn't help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if those wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and that you put on this powder which heals quickly once the burn has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of making the powder is: take one part of frankincense; two parts of dragon's blood; and three parts of live sulfur, and grind it finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the powder to the wound, and press on it firmly, until it has fully healed and is joined together with all its flesh.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it loosens, if it doesn't swell; for one shouldn't remove the medicine as long as it is not healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never make this powder of sulfur alone, if one doesn't have frankincense or dragon's blood, but only when the burn has healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the burn has already healed the wound, even to perfection, then don't put this powder on it at all.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made of wheat flour and water with honey, until it discharges pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with other treatments until it is fully healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the break of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then bind it with fine forceps.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you about broken skulls afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound comes to the neck and is simple, then it doesn't have a difference between it and that of the skull, but if the jugular vein or artery of the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's the jugular vein, then there is no other remedy than to let the wound heal and not put any constricting thing on it, because it hurts the veins and makes them recede.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the veins is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but apply warm medicine to it, such as sulfur dissolved in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber juice also dissolved in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other medicines made from myrrh in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is fully healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and swollen and full of pus, then puncture or drain them lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding comes out, then uncover it, and tie it off with a ligature, and cauterize it as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the trachea or windpipe is cut, or the esophagus, and the conduct of food is obstructed, by which the flesh goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	then sew up the trachea above the collarbone of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it gently, and leave it for some days, then treat it with ointments of old wine until it is fully healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then sew (the flesh) back in place.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, then extract them all if you can, and the parts that you cannot remove, leave them in place until the wound has purged.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and sew up and ligate the opening (of the wound).
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, then apply powder on it that I have said. (i.e. the powdered mixture made from frankincense, dragon's blood, and sulfur)
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and a fistula (abnormal connection between an organ or cavity and the skin), then treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of wounds from lances or knives.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's a wound from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, then see if there is ventilation coming from the wound, that the patient exhales: know then that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it's not deep and is fresh with all its flesh, then don't put the powder on it at first hour, nor tie it up because the blood doesn't congeal in a deep place.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and reverts to the heart, and kills the patient.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I apply attractive ointments, and bind it two times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you don't have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture and clean it.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on top of the wound for three days, or four days, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there's no spasm and no bad trembling of the heart, then it's not a sign of death drawing near.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see good signs, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat it with ointments and other treatments until it is fully healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it can't heal and close up, then know that there is a fistula (abnormal connection between an organ or cavity and the skin), and treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from a sword or knife and it's superficial, on the front or back, then treat it as one would treat an open wound in front. (i.e. follow similar treatment procedures)
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it's large, sew it up; if it's small, apply powder; and if it's pressed into the bone and has cut pieces, then sew up the wound and extract the loose fragments.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not loose, then let the wound purify itself, so that it will ligate and close up the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said. (i.e. follow the same general principles of treatment)
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a ruptured belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The rupture of the belly is great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	of the large wound there comes out sometimes the intestines, or the veins of the intestines, by which their introduction.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and sewing it up is more difficult, and sometimes worse than a small wound compared to a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because of which, one puts the intestines back in with more pins, if they are not put back together piece by piece.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell at once when they feel cold, so they do not go back in with pins.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because of this, the small wound is more favorable, because one carefully sews back the intestine to its place, with two or three stitches.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common stitches happen in the suture of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the stitch of other wounds of the body and two other proper stitches are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and in any case they are more proper with the stitch of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it. (i.e. there are three types of stitches, two of which are common to other wounds, but the third is specific to the belly)
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small and there is nothing from the intestine protruding.
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and if there's no problem putting it back in place, then it's done by one of the two manners: (i.e. either a common stitch or another proper stitch)
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said. (i.e. it's suitable for a small stitch)
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this manner: (i.e. use some method to warm up the affected area)
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak an sponge or a woolen cloth in lukewarm water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or cook it in vinegar with cypress and spike (i.e. a type of plant extract)
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and warm the intestine until the swelling is gone.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and once you have done this, the wound restrains and becomes worse, because it only swells further to become inflamed.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with water or wine and let it cook until the herbs are cooked.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because by doing this, the entry point is closed and nothing comes out.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it can't enter, then make a small opening in the wound with an instrument similar to what you use to lance boils.
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is worse than the cut itself.
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	which we should not cut unless there is a great necessity and no other way to treat it.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that's the instrument for cutting it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut into it in the curvature and not outward, and see how its shape is.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine comes out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	then put it back in place according to its natural shape in its proper location.
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power (i.e. the skill), because this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it's in the area below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it's fitting that you make the patient lie on their back.
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and put his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it's in the area below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	then put the head and the hips higher than the parts below. (i.e. to facilitate drainage)
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	then position yourself so that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it's fitting to follow what I say in large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds, apply whatever is recommended. (i.e. a different treatment)
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take in your hands a skilled surgeon who knows the entire rupture and its extent by touch.
et assemble les levres;	and sew up the lips (of the wound).
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that's the common method of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and take a needle or several, according to the size and width of the wound.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound a double thread of esparto and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread.
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two holes in the leather with the two holes of the siphac (i.e. a type of plant fiber).
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is on the inside of the leather, as long as you make it pierce from that part. (i.e. to pass through both layers)
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and tie together the two ends of the siphac in three knots.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then take a double thread and wrap it around the needle from two sides.
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	then tie together the two ends of the wound properly, (i.e. with the thread).
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave another double thread and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread just like you tied it for the first needle. (i.e. in three knots)
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not stop doing this with each needle as long as you need them.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is closed up.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and use needles of varying sizes, from small to large,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because thin needles can pierce all the flesh and very thick ones cannot enter well.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is fitting that they be of varying sizes.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it does not help to push the needles too far into the flesh and leather.
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	so that they do not pierce and widen the wound before the stitches.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the ends of the needles so that they do not scratch the patient while they are sleeping.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put ointments or cloths on the ends of the needles to keep them from coming out.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them there until the wound is sutured.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because only one needle or two are sufficient.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitch is common, (i.e. a simpler method)
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it's that you tie together the two holes of the leather and the two holes of the siphac together with a needle where there is a strong medium thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these holes all three tied,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	you sew the needle at the part where you started, in the manner that one sews clothes. (i.e. by pulling the thread tight)
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put esparto between each stitch, the thickness of a small double thread.
ceste costure sevent li home,	This stitch is known to men. (i.e. it's a common and well-known method)
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound that belonged to a man, in his belly. (i.e. an example of this stitch being used successfully)
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife.
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm in width, (i.e. quite large)
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were well protruding two palms in width.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was inside the belly. (i.e. an internal injury)
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestine, and it had been outside for 24 hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sutured in just 15 days, healed, and fully recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the barber had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; (i.e. a remarkable outcome)
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not cure him with ointment, because I was in a place where one could not find any, nor any medicine. (i.e. a challenging situation)
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I applied old cotton on top of the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was fully healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper methods of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and push it from the outside part to the inside part.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the leather in a straight line, then tie the end of the siphac or costet to where you have inserted the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side, from inside out to outside again.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew in the same way that a furrier sews furs, (i.e. with a similar technique)
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and you leave the siphac on one side and take it up again from the other, until the stitching is fully completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, which Galien says properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is the way in which some people sew together the two parts naturally, (i.e. without sewing through both layers)
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one of the ends of the siphac to the other end, in this manner: (i.e. tying them together)
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or thread from close by, and make it pierce only that spot.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the siphac. (i.e. without tying them together)
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle around and make it pierce from the outside part to the inside part. (i.e. completing the stitch)
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	with both ends of the siphac. (i.e. finishing the stitch with the two loose threads)
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce from the outside part to the inside part, in two other holes of the mirach that are on the other side. (i.e. completing the stitch with additional threads)
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second manner of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien himself said these words, and many people testify to them. (i.e. confirming the effectiveness of this stitch)
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one should sew the belly with two needles, each with thread in it; (i.e. using both threads to secure the stitching)
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets. (i.e. using a similar technique to secure the threads)
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is inside the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it's a more grievous stitch than in other parts of the belly. (i.e. a more serious injury)
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgments of a wound are such as those of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood, so that fire has altered it,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you put back the intestine and the gut, then lay on powdered charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if fire has altered it, then put on any ointment that is available, until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and sew up the flesh and the skin.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicine, put on old cotton, as soon as it begins to heal.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and turn it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need of other medicine in most simple cases of wounds;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound makes a commotion to the main members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	so it is convenient for you to moisten linen light with warm temperate oil or rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the swellings, and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if it feels pain or festering in the bowels, and many times happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	so give enemas of black vinegar, and indeed if the festering comes just up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more easily healed than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jun" cannot heal when it is hurt,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it's because of the narrowness of their veins that they are, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to that of nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestines burst from the wound, put them back in place just like the intestine, while it is fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become green or black, it is convenient that you tie the part that is black so that no bleeding comes from it.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cover what is between the stitches,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put both threads hanging from the part under the wound all the way to the outside to lighten the extraction when the intestines break and the wound bursts.
de la routure dou boueil	of the great suffering of the belly.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some people,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen a man wounded in the belly by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and it was the wound to the right of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and he was sewn up and became a fistula, and from that there came an abscess and festering.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him as I knew how and did not cease to subtlety until he was healed, and the wound closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it close, I doubted that the sickness had turned into an abscess in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no evil, but he stayed in better disposition, and eating and drinking normally.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and the experienced ones said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be stitched up in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fresh linen and great stitches, then assemble the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the linen has turned the mouth outwards, put it on both lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it encloses its mouth shut;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then cover the head, and it stays so that he cannot untie.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another piece of linen behind in this same manner as before, until the wound is completely enclosed;
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	That treatment keeps the person from suffering in the intestine, and brings no harm to him;
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and it is possible to sew the intestine with a fine thread that has been prepared from the intestine of an animal.
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take one end of this intestinal thread which is well cleaned,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the other end of that thread a fine linen thread twisted into a cord.
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then put the thread in the needle and sew up the intestine, and then trim it in the natural way;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of sewing with linen is not far from being according to the way of faith and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, or even in one of the main intestines, then there is no remedy nor cure, but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers and gets worse, is universally called a "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and especially when it bursts and flows freely.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the hardness of the firm and white nodule, or where there is no sense of pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it also bursts like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it flows freely and other times becomes thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and other times a lot.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and there is no scar,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is none other than by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, either by the smallness of the blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or because it is malignant.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scar tissue inside and on the edges of the wound that does not allow new flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because it has too much pus.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or because the wound is corrupt and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or because the medicine used in the treatment was not good.
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague or pestilence.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of the property in that region, where digestion is slow and healing is also slow, and nature follows a bad course.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or because there are veins or bones involved.
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicine in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is fitting for me to tell you about the treatment of a fistula that is done by handwork, or manual surgery.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in every part of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	because there are fistulas that come to the great veins, and the arteries, and the nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the bladder, or to the intestines, or to the kidneys, or to any of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and such that it comes to the principal part and similar parts of the body.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are in this manner are of great difficulty in healing, and there is no remedy but surgery and ignorance does not help.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the point I have mentioned, and you have faith in the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it is possible to understand, take a lead or iron thread, and if the fistula is straight, then bind it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is curved, then search for a fine thread of silk.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	because the silk bends easily around the curvature.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well thread it with threads,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it through one of the openings.
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	because the cleansing liquid runs from one opening to another and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then bind it tightly with string, according to your skill, if there are bones or nerves within and it is bursting open.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the sick person carefully about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where exactly he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, then cover it as I have instructed.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the dead flesh and corrupt scars that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deep and open in a straight place, it is necessary that you cover it completely, as much as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put wet threads soaked in medicated water and insert them up to the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine dissolves the remaining superfluity that is left at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I apply ointments of good salve until they are completely healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if they are not healed by that, then I would cauterize them as we have said.
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves are in the way or touching the principal part of the body, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is exposed and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it clean until all the corruption is removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with good ointments until it is completely healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it does not heal and bursts again as before.
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you have not reached the root of the problem:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	if it bursts and opens up, then bind it tightly until you reach the bottom.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then restore the place to its original state.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is healed in this way, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep and you cannot come to its root;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy but the surgeon's skill by nature.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can grasp it with forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then pull it out with an instrument suitable for that purpose.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then remove them all together, not leaving any one behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the moisture (pus) makes it difficult and there is no room for error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then cover it up with ointment and cloth, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on the wound some salve to purify it.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the place around the bones is completely rotten and putrid.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will come out more easily.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as the femur or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then scrape away only the corruption until all the blackness is removed.
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of the corrupted bone that comes close to the marrow of the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	then it is necessary to scrape and cover all up until the corruption, and then treat it until it is completely healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in one man's leg.
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and aid from this workmanship.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	so that the matter came out to the leg and became inflamed with a large abscess, and there was no apparent reason for it to open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the barber-surgeons, through their ignorance, cut too close to the abscess and opened it.
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and a lot of matter came out and became a fistula, and there were many openings that all flowed with pus from the body.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many surgeons attempted to treat it for two years, but there was no skill in manual surgery.
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	until I was called and came to see his leg and the remedies with which they were treating him.
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what was coming out from the openings was a large, thick mass.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red and had a yellowish-green hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I inserted a thread into one of the openings and then threaded all the openings.
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that they were connected to each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I then hurried and plugged up one of the openings as far as I could until I exposed a part of the bone.
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it was corrupted and perforated, and the corruption came right to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I scraped away what was appearing from the corrupted bone, and I believed that there was no other corruption except for what I had removed.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and then I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, but it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I started again, and scraped away the bone as before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found that the corruption continued in the bone, so I scraped it away and then removed it, and I worked to close the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not, until I wrapped a palm's width of the bone in a dressing and pulled it out to its entirety.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored him with medicines, and he was healed and sound quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it did not need to be done again except for the weakness of the sick person who could not bear.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often due to the evacuation of blood, but he was completely healed.
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and in place of the bone grew hard and firm flesh, and he was in good health with no harm or opposition from anything at all, neither while eating nor while coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, it must be scraped away in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a linen cloth and place it at the head of the bone that has opened up.
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and tell someone to extend it upwards.
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and take another linen cloth, larger than the first one, and place it over the flesh that is above the bone.
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch it so that you can pull out the corrupt flesh from underneath.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and expose the flesh on the place where you see fit to scrape, so that the scraping does not damage the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a red-hot iron or a hot plate underneath the bone to melt the corrupt flesh.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to scrape until you can see and feel the corruption, and then scrape again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	then scrape away all the flesh, and then place a red-hot iron underneath.
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then scrape out the corruption from one part to another, and make sure the scraping is done all along the length of the corruption, just as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in a joint, then cut away the corrupted joint and scrape out the bone where it contains from the other side.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other remedy but to cut through them both.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in a finger of the hand or a toe, it must be very strong to deal with that thing.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless you should investigate how that corruption presents itself.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways you can, but beware of the vein or nerve that might get in your way.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the knives and scrapers for cutting those bones are many, depending on the shape of the bone and its appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and because of this it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each type of surgery according to its resemblance.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work itself will show you the instrument you will need, in accordance with your knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the symptoms of illnesses.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so that you can think about the instrument you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	with fire.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The eyes can become infected or damaged from within, or by an external cause.
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have used medicine to treat the corruption and it does not help.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut off that member up to the place where the corruption comes from.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the sick person escapes either by death or by the more severe evil of losing the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, so that it seems to be burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then it becomes putrid after the blackness, and the corruption of the member spreads from member to member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold of the whole body, so you must hasten to cut away.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the bite of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is at the head of the vein, then cut it off, and do not give it space to come as far as the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes as far as the hand, then cut off at the joint, so that the corruption does not come as far as the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then cut off at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, that is death.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there's no remedy other than the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do the same with the foot when corruption comes to it: if it reaches the first joint, cut after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it reaches the foot, then cut off the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends to the leg, then cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy but for the patient to die from it.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the way of cutting or scraping the member is that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and have one servant stretch out the lower part of the linen downwards, and another servant hold the other linen upwards.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you expose the flesh that is between the two linens to the length of a spatula wide, so that the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or scrape it, and put a linen cloth from each side, so that the scraping does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another wound and abscess will come to the sick person.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding comes out during your operation, then cauterize the place immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	You put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and heal it until it is sound;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to me in my own person:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	a burn that seemed like it was from fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this burning came first to the two front feet, until it had taken over all of the foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the burn, he hastily covered the foot and was healed;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and after a long time afterwards the burn came back to his two hands, and he came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things that would counteract the corruption of the body after it had been purged, and the burnings could not cease;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he asked me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of reversing the material;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die;
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the strength of the man was weak; and he lost all hope and returned to his land,
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastily covered his hand and was healed;
