et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not told this story except to show what others do in similar cases, if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never does a carbuncle come to a place so soft and fatty that it remains for so long that it gathers a great gathering of boils;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then they burst and perforate, and the boils jump out, and the place remains empty, just like a vessel that has been emptied.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin on top is as delicate as a fine silk cloth;
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and they do not spread to the bone or to the nerve, and such an illness is called "healthy";
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes to the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is like when you cut that skin all around, and similarly when it is delicate, just like a cloth;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it does not heal because of its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have hope that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in depth,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then close it with a poultice;
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	examine if the abscess is large and the boils that come out have a foul smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then apply the Egyptian ointment made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take aloe, oil, and litharge, in equal parts, and put the mixture into a vessel on the fire;
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	so that the medicine is red and thickens to be as viscous as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from it according to your need, and mix it with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and apply the poultice to the abscess, and close the opening.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay on for two hours, then remove it by pressing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the abscess is cleansed and the foul odor is removed.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and once was ointmented with ash water;
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and you take ashes from the wood of a vine, and pour water over them;
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then strain it, and apply it as a poultice, until you know that the abscess is thoroughly cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the sick person cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian ointment nor ash water;
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	so apply a poultice of honey and water, or with a little bit of litharge in it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or apply the poultice made from honey and sweet wine, for honey has the property of cleansing and purifying.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine helps to heal the wound.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this and have hope that the abscess is thoroughly cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then apply the poultice of these things, so that flesh may grow in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take diaphanit plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine;
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or apply a poultice made from various medicines and ointments, the properties of which I have previously mentioned or described in the treatment of ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the abscess is small and the stick of the poultice cannot enter;
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then stretch it with a needle a little bit, and put on a cloth with Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or apply Basilicon ointment until it is stretched;
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then sew it up and leave only one small opening through which the poultice can enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the opening from which boils come out is on top, then cut or lower it so that it is;
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the boil is deep, it will not let flesh grow in.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut open the abscess from below as you wish,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then arrange it in such a way that the boil runs down to its lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	for when the boil is deep, it will not allow flesh to grow;
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut open the abscess from below as you wish,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so arrange it in such a way that the boil runs lightly downwards, and leave nothing of the boil.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the abscess,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and then spread a linen cloth over it that covers the entire abscess.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut at the strongest point of the opening of the abscess, making it one notch wider than before.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then apply a soothing ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening;
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on top of the abscess to lighten the boil, and do not remove the large cloth outside until after many days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that one which is on top of the opening of the abscess, take it off often to remove the boil.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes out from the boil, whether it is venom or pus, enough or too much, digestible or indigestible.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there are any ulcers or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your treatment has spread in this manner and you see the kind of thing that comes out on top of the abscess,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the abscess is healing well, and approach the patient's recovery.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loose it on the morning of the third day, and when you remove the dressing from the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	replace the other cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the abscess continues to discharge foul pus after many days, know that the abscess is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venom comes out after a long time, do not despair of recovery,
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health is approaching. For there are men who take a long time to grow flesh in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if foul pus comes out of the abscess after many days, know that the abscess is not healing.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the abscess takes a long time to heal and becomes suppurating, add drying medicines in consistency and virtues.
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphanit ointment, for it has a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	Take diaphanit ointment, and mix it with rose oil, and equal parts of old wine in consistency.
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then melt it and use it; and make the same mixture with cooked and thickened honey.
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when diaphanit ointment is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloe and incense, grind them together, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then make a paste with this cloth, and apply it to the abscess, and administer it every night for a long time.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and the roots of celestial lily, which is also like flour from violets and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use them in simple or composite forms: grind them, make a powder of them, and put it on the honey that I have mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is long-lasting and not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption has gone deep into the bone, or to the hard limbs, or to the sinews.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	for the treatment of this abscess is similar to the treatment of a fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the ulcer of the foot or ankle.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pannerium is an ulcer that forms under the nail of the thumb,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or on the foot, or perhaps it appears in other fingers.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is neglected and has become old, then a foul ulcer comes to it.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and runs and discharges pus as far as the root of the nail, and perhaps all around.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to corrosion right up to the bone, so that it causes a foul-smelling pain, and the joints of the fingers are swollen, and the skin is discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the section on treatment, and the treatment does not help,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut off the entire excess of the nail which remains from the ulcer.
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the nail presses against the flesh and begins to rot and ulcerate.
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put a dressing under the nail that touches the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it on top and carefully cut off the subtle and delicate flesh.
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything;
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out and treat the wound afterwards, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the joint corrupting, then cut it out in two pieces just as it was said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed and swollen, and it hurts a lot, then it is necessary that you first treat the swelling.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut off the nail of the spur in a diagonal manner from above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and take care that the cut does not reach to the flesh under the nail, for the sick person would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something on it that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand;
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The joints that appear on some men's hands, perhaps because they are all flesh.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps it is so shaped that there are bones in it, and sometimes there is a nail;
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them appear at the root of the joint, or the birthplace is in one of the bones of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that are born in any part of the bone of the finger do not become numb;
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that are born at the joint of the finger, perhaps it becomes numb.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of one who is fleshy is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it off at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint is difficult to cure, if you do not take care to cut it off.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In that which is born or grows at the very end of the bone, it is necessary to cut away the flesh all around up to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cut off the bone with an appropriate tool for this case, and then treat it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The numbness that comes to the fingers together comes by birth, or by the closing of a wound, or by scorching of fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cut out that numbness, so that the joint can be repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or moistened cloths in rose oil, so that it does not become numb again.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of linen, until the place is sewn up, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If numbness comes to any of his fingers with the palm, then cut out that numbness as it is necessary.
Des vils	of warts.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Warts are ugly, swollen growths filled with melancholy excess, which come to various members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they happen more often in the legs of those who walk and work and bear loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	So it is necessary that you administer to them once purging of gall, and then cleanse with the oil of balsam.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of iron warts is in two ways: one is to cut them out and then treat the wound with black salve;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is to lift up the wart and then clean it thoroughly.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cut is done in this way: first arise the leg with hot iron very strong, so that the skin becomes fine and thin;
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then stretch out the leg of the sick person from above the knee as far as the part under the knee joint.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut off the wart in one place, or in two places, or in three places, with a wide cut.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then bind and treat the wound with black salve to your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the sick person's wound can bear.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it and command him to eat foods that are making black gall;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin the evacuation and the cleaning when the warts are full and are causing harm to the sick person.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The removal of hair is in this way: shave the leg of the sick person, if there are many hairs.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath and arise the leg with hot iron as hot as it can be made, until the hairs become red and swollen;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it over the fire and then shave in one place the wart from the long hair of the knee joint, or in the part under the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then burn the skin with the hot iron and scrape off the wart from each side, until it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then put a strip of cloth under it, as long as it is raised from the skin, and then burn it with a light iron.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut off in another place above three fingers, and then scrape the skin on the wart as far as it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it up to the strip, just as you did before, and burn it with another iron, just as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut out another strip, or more if you need them, then lift it up and cut it at the toe of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then treat and lift up to the second strip; then stretch from strip to strip until it comes out completely, and then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot pull it out and lift it up, then put a needle into each thread, strong and doubled,
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and bind it and pull it out, and put it under the strip, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not cut, because if it cuts, then one cannot pull it or lift it out, and it will cause harm to the sick person.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have pulled it out completely, then put on the wound a moistened linen cloth with wine and rose oil; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the warts are together, twisted, and swollen, and they are not straight, as we have said.
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary to split them apart, but do not cut them off; and treat them just as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron used to cut the wart is curved, so that it does not slice or cut too deep and harm the skin.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is of a thick curvature, because if it were fine, it would cut too deep into the skin; but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape.
De la voinne civile	Of the common wart.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This wart grows on the legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and on land that is dry and has little moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and perhaps it grows in other parts of the body besides the legs, and this happens because of the filth that comes from under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as it comes from worms and serpents within the body, growing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this wart are that it comes in the leg as a great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and begins to form a wart like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the swelling opens up, it is necessary to wrap around a piece of linen 3/4 of an ell (a unit of measurement) all the way up to 2 ells, and bind it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and let the linen remain on the leg, and every time it gets loose, you should rewrap around the linen and bind it again.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part of it, and rewrap around the remaining part, but do not cut it at its root until it comes out completely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it off, it will go back into the flesh and cause an ulcer or a foulness to form at the site, and a bad disease will come of it.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	on account of which thing it is necessary that she be treated little by little until the end, and that there remain no part of it in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this wart when it is treated can be as long as 5 palms or 10.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and I had one man come to me, from whom it came out as long as 10 palms, and when you cut it, it pours a stream of blood all the way down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and the matter inside is emptied, and medicine to prevent any fouling or purulence is given to the site, then it is cured just as if it were an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at any time this vein is cut open, and especially when it opens up in the joint of the foot, or between the toes.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and if there is much pus and the vein bursts; then cure it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between skin and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This illness is called in our land "disease of the oxen" because it has happened many times to bulls.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes up and down through the entire body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it is felt very well from limb to limb until it breaks through the skin where it goes and bursts out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by infection of some bad humors, just like come tapeworms and serpents and lice and worms in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts about its evilness, because when it goes through the body, it rises to the head and comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it enters, and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and pulled out, there is no doubt that it was indeed in there.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so then tie the place above and below with a strong string tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then apply some kind of poultice on top and pull it out forcefully, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you can't find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	so then cauterize it with fire above, until it blisters.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it causes is that it can blind the eye, as we have said before.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming close to the head near the eye, then tie a thread underneath it in a circle, then apply something on top and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use a cleansing medicine for the body to purify the bad humors that are causing the illness.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of spoiled meat which is putrid.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	From the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that occurs in some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then it moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to an ill woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the middle of her upper arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after that, I saw it rise up as well to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything else, just like quicksilver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departed from that place and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then soon after it ran through all the body, until it came to the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was turning around the body, just like I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease spread in that way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often seen many people move their pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it like that, as I saw in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought it was because the woman's body was weak and her veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and that's why this inflammation appeared more easily.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and they don't appear in those who are delicate and have moist bodies and well-covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease being cured, and the sick person feels that pain, if she tells you in such a way as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then you should cut up and down hastily, and then cover it so that the inflammation subsides to its former place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you don't see improvement in yourself,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if the treatment of those who suppress inflammation is used, like bitter pills and viper pills and similar things.
Des saiettes	Arrows! (it looks like you're just listing a word now)
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points and small ones, hairy and soldered [i.e., with a metal point or tip].
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those that have two angles, and those that have tongues, and those in which there are splinters.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one that strikes a limb can strike in two ways: either it strikes the principal member, or it strikes through a secondary part.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, liver, kidney, womb, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it strikes any part of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you about next, appear:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so beware of extracting this arrow, because death comes afterwards in many ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if you don't see this bad sign and the arrow is not deeply lodged, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow pierces it and penetrates the bone, and makes the sputum burst forth which is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	and the sign of this is that you have a scotoma and swoon and vertigo and redness in your eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and commotion of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it bursts forth from the nostrils or the ears; and perhaps it harms speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is discharge of a moist white pus, like an abscess, and also as if from a boil on the skin.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you see this sign, be careful of the treatment, and extract the arrow if it's not too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it strikes the liver is that it is near the left nipple, and feels like it was stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow becomes gangrenous like an abscess, and causes black blood, and comes with cold sweat and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	know then without doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow when it strikes the navel is that foamy discharge bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and sighs loudly and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes the covering of the liver, it is near the small ribs; and there is great anguish and great pain, and sighing; and all the muscles of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow strikes the stomach, perhaps there is discharge from the wound of something undigested flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes the belly and there is a discharge of feces through the intestines, then there is no hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow strikes the bladder, and urine flows out and comes forth, and the sick person feels a very great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and wrists and knees and toes, and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it's not venomous, as I will tell you that happened to me, for that reason.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one of my friends who was struck by an arrow in the armpit near the neck root.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and drew it out from another side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any noticeable harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrow that had struck in the fat of the eye under the eyebrow.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was stuck, and I could only get a hold of the tip towards the shaft.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the arrow was great as an Turkish bowstring, to all light iron without ears; the game was healed, and there came no bad accident.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with fletching (ears).
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I bound the head (of the arrow) with bandages, and softened it as much as I could, and then pulled it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out an arrow from one of my men, who had been struck in the stomach and whom I thought was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after he passed 30 days, his condition did not change at all.
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut away above the arrow, and enclosed it, and pulled it out without any bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see one man to whom an arrow has struck in the back, and the wound was sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural condition.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor did he find any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see one other man to whom an arrow struck him in the face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out an arrow from one of the king's princes, who had it struck in the nape of his neck.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was leaning slightly to the right side; and the arrow was completely stuck.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to treat it three days after it had been struck. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it with all a subtle probe, and did not find it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt a prickling sensation and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied a plaster that is attracting and digestive to the wound, so that the swelling would not increase.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the tip of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied a plaster again for three days, and the wound healed back up again, and the sick person remained thus for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the arrow one day inside his neck, and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied to the wound a medicinal concoction that is corrosive for three days, until it was completely open.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrow which was corroding at the wound.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted into the opening of the wound that corrosive medicine, until the tip of the arrow became visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and the tip passed completely through in about four months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I closed up the wound and applied tongs to one side and the other, and it could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not stop trying and inventing various devices with instruments, until I managed to grasp it one day with well-made tongs.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	in accordance with what its shape will come at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the doctors judged that the nasal septum cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the sick person was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows.
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you can put your treatment on what I do not say, because books cannot possibly contain everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters learn from small things and from what is present and defective.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	find new works and new instruments in the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not come out from members where they are stuck unless by two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the place where they enter, or through another side.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that one which comes out through the other side is a arrow entering into fleshy parts and never comes out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, then let it stay until the flesh is rotten around it, and the exit is opened up.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and similarly if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, then let it stay for some days, and turn it each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it will come out, and if it does not come out, then pierce around with a very fine needle, so that the area around is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the ventricles of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the sick person: do not pull it out at all, but let it stay until it becomes equal in size after a few days.
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow reaches the brainpan, that's the death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself and does not reach the brainpan,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and the sick person remains for a few days without bad accidents, if he encloses it to be pulled out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck in this way and cannot come out, then I administer herbs around, as I have told you, then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is stuck in the flesh of the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it with all caution.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then pull it out with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot due to the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein in its way, then cut it until the wound becomes large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are fletching on the arrow that hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	then remove the flesh that is stuck to both parts of the arrow as much as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the fletching of the arrow so that you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the arrow itself, for then you would have to remove it more painfully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't pull it out in one go, then let it stay until the area around is rotten, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be opened up.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the hemorrhaging of blood makes things worse, then administer what we have said about treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be careful of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and think up a device as to how you can pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the sick person in the same shape as he was when the arrow struck him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for that is the greatest aid that can be done for him; and if you cannot do it, then put him in the position that the signs show to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes out from another side, or it shows some sign of its presence, or the skin is swollen in the area where one can see or feel it distinctly.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	then cut up to that point, so that the tongs can take hold of it, and then pull it out; if it comes out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, so that it enters into the bone, and enlarge the bone, and then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, then let it be for a while longer, and then continue the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the shaft of the arrow is there, then insert all the shaft into it.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the shaft breaks and you see fit to administer binding, then apply one instrument that is chewed.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters into the chewed part of the instrument, and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck, then insert one instrument with an entering point into it, to ease out the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is embedded, then it is well for you to cut all around the flesh where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow breaks off in the chest or belly or bladder or intestines and is near, and you can cut above it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, pull out the arrow, and then close the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to remove arrows are similar to the beak of a bird, and look at this shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, small, and little ones, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the chewed plug is also like a bird's feather.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	in order to push into the point of the arrow, as shown by this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for pushing and checking if it is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of common body veins.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of the veins from which one bleeds, there are 31, and in the head there are 16.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say, two plexuses that are after the ears, which are called the "two herpethe".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in the two apparent temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and two veins that are in the two corners of the eyes, which are called "aspisres".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is in the forehead, and the vein that is at the back of the neck.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lips above the mouth, and they are called "augerich" veins.
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The common veins from which one bleeds in each arm are five.
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, and it is on the left side of the chest, and common people call it the "vein of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called the "basilic", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and common people call it the "vein of the heart", and the basilic vein is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and common people call it the "vein of the belly", and it is above the scrotum.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and it is that vein which bleeds, which appears clearly in front of the penis.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvadore vein is the vein that is between the auricular and the annular veins, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one of which is beneath the fold of the skin on the left side of the thigh,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one is the saphenous vein, which is at the ankle of the right side, and the vein that is called "saphene", which is in the other ankle.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins beneath those ones.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears helps against the ancient cathars and against migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the bleeding, as I told you, is that you raise the head of the sick person,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with an abrasive cloth, then compress the sick person's neck with a vice.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until the two veins behind the ears appear in their respective places beneath the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	and then ask your doctor to sign it, and where you feel the pulse under your arm, that is where he will sign.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and insert it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand in such a way that the vein flows upwards.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and release the skin and vein on both sides of the groove, and let out as much blood as you see fit.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind it up and leave it alone, until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already mentioned the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is worth against ancient migraine.
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and for sore eyes and habitual ophthalmia, and for sharp pain in the corners of the eyes.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of a surgeon so is as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient strains his neck, so much so that the two tendons appear openly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the pulse below your elbow, and then signs [that it is] gone;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the curet above the tendon on top of your wrist bone, and push the lancet underneath;
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the tendon up, and cut it, just like you have done with the other two tendons, and make a clean cut through the blood according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and put your hand on the tendon for an hour, then put a compress on;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then the tendon will bind together, and leave it alone until it is healed; and thus we have spoken of its cutting and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the tendon of the forehead is worth as much as the healing of the cephatic artery in ancient diseases of the face and in migraine and in rheum.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is that the patient strains his neck in twisting, so much so that the tendon appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip above the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let two bloodlets issue according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then tie a knot in the patient's arm and bind the vein until it is cut off and every time you do an operation make a wide ligature.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it does not seem right that the ligatures are too tight; and the vein is cut across, because the bone is close, and perhaps the ligature breaks when it becomes thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The cutting of the two veins that are in the two arms is greatly helpful to them, and to jaundice, and to gout, and to redness in the eye, and to diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their bleeding is that the patients stretch out their neck twisting with some kind of ligature, just as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then bleed, and let the bleeding be from the traverse, a piece of the length of the ligature a piece wide, because it has no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the ligatures are thin, perhaps they will break; then do what you must to stop the bleeding, and then tie on a layer of cloth, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The bleeding of the vein of the neck is worth against ague, and against dropsy, and against diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient stretches out their neck, then takes hold of their nose with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the thin and long ligature, and insert it in the space between the two nostrils, near the lip.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the veins do not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and don't go too far inside, and let the bleeding of the blood flow as much as you need it, then tie it up for one night, because it is quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and that's the shape of the ligature:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The bleeding of the two groin veins is helpful against constriction of the limbs, and against starting to swell, and against many diseases, and against inflammation, and against gangrene, and against ulcers, and against itching eruptions.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient stretches out their neck under one and then under the other, just as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be sitting on the head of the patient, and the patient sit on one stool.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then bleed the vein of the long part somewhat widely, then draw out the blood temperately, or as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other part in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and strain out the blood moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient does not choke; and let it be until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	On the bleeding of the lips.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins of the upper lips helps against boils in the mouth, and against corruption of the gums, and cracks of the lips, and also around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is that you make the patient sit in front of you, and stretch out their neck as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right upper lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and you can recognize them by what they are black, and by what there are small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	cut then one and the other, and if you do not recognize them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then cut the largest of each side, and do exactly the same with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	On the bleeding under the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The veins under the tongue help after the purging of the head; it's for the constriction of the throat, and the diseases of the eye, and the diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the purifier is that the sick person sees between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	then purify both of them, and do not go too deep because under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the throat which are commonly purged are purged in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with a burning and fiery mint leaf, or a subtle olive-like pinching like those cutting threads, and it is called "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the burning mint is very well-known, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it has to open the veins which are full of thick, flowing blood and that contain thick and troubled blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive-like burning mint:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle in its pinching, and is for purifying the subtle veins, where there is a subtle, yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The purifying of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with illnesses that are under the throat, and neck, and chest, and belly.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is convenient for the purifier to purge carefully, and to beware of the artery that lies underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he strikes the artery and bleeding starts coming out, then the purifier must staunch it, as I said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and he should not be pinching with the burning mint, but rather cutting it like anesil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilic vein does not open visibly, then the purifier should extract it and change to another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or if you want any part of it, or if you purge in place of it the vein inside the arm: it opens visibly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and you strike with the burning mint, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you see the place of the purging, then it is necessary to extract the arm, that you touch the place as far as you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place of the incision, and then bind the arm, and strike the vein with the burning mint anesil.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and be careful not to hit the artery when you see the place swollen, because it is the artery: withdraw then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come out upwards like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is blood from the artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and put your hand up high, then take your hand away if the bleeding has stopped, for it often happens many times.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	bind the arm and leave it so, and do not move the ailing one; and be on guard, and do not move them until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is not stopped and it comes back, and medicine is not present to you, then strike the artery if it opens up, because the head of the vein retreats; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a husk of figs, cut it open, and take one of the halves and bind it tightly up to the other joint;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the bleeding stops, that's good. If not, then cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of the bleeding is not grievous in many dispositions for the small extent of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The purging of the vein in the middle helps to treat blood from the head above and the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is convenient for the purifier to be careful about the nerve that lies underneath, and if he strikes too deep, then he finds the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the patient is grievous, and by chance cannot be healed.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve opens up many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you must take out the purifier with anesil instrument; and withdraw the nerve at your ability.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has vein between the two nerves, then cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The purging of the cephalic vein helps to draw blood from the head and benefits them.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is convenient to purge with the burning olive oil or the burning myrtle, because it is the most safe of all veins, since it does not have underneath either nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the most superficial location, and do nothing if you fail at first time, and repeat.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the locations swell in some men when you fail at first time, but it does not harm them.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the purging is according to your opinion. (This suggests that the text is acknowledging the limitations and variations in medical practices, and leaving room for individual interpretation.)
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about purging is that purging is not done in excess, but only to preserve health. (This suggests that the text is emphasizing moderation and balance in medical treatment.)
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future illnesses;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the purging be done in one of the three veins that are commonly used: namely, the cephalic, fist, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it should be purged in the beginning of spring, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and it should be purged on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The purging that is administered for illnesses has no fixed hour determined, but when the need arises, day or night, in all hours and in all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not necessary to purge children until they are 14 years old, nor women who have more than the fourth month's gestation up to the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years be purged.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wants to purge themselves, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that they cleanse the intestines with a light cathartic.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if there are many fetid humors retained, so that the veins do not draw out the superfluities which are hurtful to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should those who are too salivated with meats, or drunken, be purged as long as they remain so, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and be careful not to purge after a passion of colic, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and multiple habitations with women, and labor, watching, and working at night, and all that is due to virtue, or by reason of arms or body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtlety the humors, if the blood is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the ability.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then take a bath, or sweat it out, if no other thing hinders, to subtlety the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and purify yourself from the vein of the abdomen around the third time, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day free from work, and labor, and lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be joyful and happy, and let the purifier be higher than he who is being purified, and rub his arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then bind the ligature above gently, because if it is too tight or loose, it cannot stop the blood.
