et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the place with hands, until the veins swell and can be felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the purifier with the flame of an old oil pot, then put the tip of his left hand on top of the vein under the place where he wants to purge.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burn and fail when pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	Because there are veins that are as slippery as cords when being purged, and some of these have an abundance of air in them.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when the flame is put on it, it retires from the flame, and cannot be opened up, and thus are those veins.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if the vein closes again, it is because the wound was too tight, for that reason the purifier should be advised in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein does not close the first time, it is good; and if not, then repeat again a little below that place or above hastily, if the swelling has not appeared.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the place is swollen and the sickness spreads, let it be left for one or two days, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	perhaps there will come purulent swellings; do not take a bath, then repeat the purging if it seems to please him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the opening is small, or the blood flows subtly and you doubt that it does not flow as much as you see, then pour all the flame directly into that opening itself.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and it will work quickly, so that the place becomes swollen; because this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the place swollen, do not repeat the purging, and put a little of olive oil on it, because it lightens the body of blood and is more beneficial in this place than oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer olive oil in every purging that you make of the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and this same thing makes triacle and powder of water, when it is put on the place; it subtles the blood and separates it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there come large purulent swellings, which have happened many times, namely when it is not been purified for a long time or the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	then hurry and put on the place a wet sponge in hot water and vinegar for a short while, and then squeeze it out for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the issue of blood from the vein, and if there remains on the place after some days any blackness or greenness, it does not harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see anything, put on something made from aloes or myrrh mixed with vinegar of marjoram, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there has been purulent appearance at the site of purging from the basilic vein: therefore put your hand on it and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, it is that bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Be careful then that you do not put anything on it of what we have said, for perhaps there will be bleeding from the artery; but make one dry plaster to harden the place, and then apply another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And value each blood according to its quantity of virtue, and its color.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the blood is black, let it come out until it becomes red; and if you see a lot of it, let it come out until it thins out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is full and strong, and needs to be bled, that the cut should be made larger, and the opening of the vein should be wider.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and have him purged little by little, and it should be necessary to purge him with a diagonal cut, not with a sharp one.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this way of purging is safe from hemorrhaging and severing the nerve, and is worth more than the purging of length or width.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for one whose body is weakened by the purging, it is necessary to give him a wet poultice in juice of ripe lemons; if he is overheated, then draw out three or four times as much blood.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if he has a cold complexion, then anoint him with a wet poultice in sweet syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and very fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if he is troubled after the purging, after a lot of blood has come out, it is necessary that he inhale broth of meat and subtle, fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things that we have said in the chapter on swooning, for evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm and purge again, it is necessary, when he is weakened by great purging, that he should purge little by little, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to empty his arm again after the first purging, and he has a strong body, then he should purge 7 hours after the first purging, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if someone wants to be purified in another way, then they should be purged the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because there is a lot of blood inside the body that has already been heated and caused fever; it is necessary to draw out a great quantity and enlarge the opening so much that it comes in through the armpit.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you must reap all the benefits of purging, and put your hand on his pulse when he is purged, so that the mortification does not come in through the armpit.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times when the purifier is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary to loosen the arm and let blood out the second time, and have the opening closed, that you press strongly on it.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is curved, should he stretch his arm hastily, for this would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him leave it until he purges the second time; or you can insert the tip of the flame into the opening, so that the blood which has been chilled at the vein comes out freely.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on a little vinegar mixed with water, and press on it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be left alone and do not bind it tightly, until the purulent swelling has been calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw out blood the second time, let him purge in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins on the arm are purged instead of those in the head, because they are composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of the purging is that the sick person puts his hand in hot water until the finger-nails are red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it is tied gently so that the vein appears well, and then he purges now diagonally, not lengthwise or widthwise.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the opening be wide and let it be purged well near the joint of the hand, and if the blood cannot come out, then put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is winter, do not put your hand in hot water again, because you have made it colder than summer already.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the purging of this vein is safer from all other veins, because there is no artery or nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The purging of the vein on the right hand's wrist is worth to all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	extend the hand and put it in hot water until the vein becomes swollen and can be seen.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if you purify diagonally and cut through the whole thing completely, then nothing will harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep because the nerves are under all the muscles of the flesh.
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as is necessary for you, then put oil and vinegar on the vein to close it up quickly, and do this with each of them.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The purging in the left hand is worth for the disease of the spleen, and do exactly as I told you to do with the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The purging of the hypogastric vein is worth for all the diseases that are under the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the uterus, retention of menses, disease of the womb, and old diseases of the thighs and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its purging is that the sick person puts their foot in hot water and rubs on the vein until it bursts.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and tie a cloth over the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and there are many veins that go up from the foot.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then purify the one that is in the most prominent or largest vein, or at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you purify on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are under it, and purify diagonally also as if cutting; and have the flame very close.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water again, and let it drain well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the purifier fails the first time, then repeat the second time above a little bit, because the place is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	nor do not doubt nerves, as we have said, and do the same with the hypogastric vein of the other foot in a similar way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The place of the sciatic vein is at the knee, and its purging is worth for the pain in the groin, when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its purging is that the sick person gets into a bath and stretches above the knee 4 fingers in twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise the vein will not appear; and if it appears, then purify in all ways that you can, and diagonally.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and is worth more than cutting, because the place is salty, and it is very sensitive to the touch of hands themselves.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it, then purify any vein that appears on the back of the foot or towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do so until the blood flows freely, then loosen the tie and put on cotton and compress it; she is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	The purgings of the syringe
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made from horns, or copper, or glass; and leeching is done in two ways: either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this leeching which is done without piercing is in two ways: either it is all heat, or no heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and leeching which is done by piercing and extraction of blood is made in fourteen places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which one is all on the head, and the others are between the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in the sides of the neck; and a leech under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and a leech on each shoulder; and a leech above the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and leeches in both arms; and leeches in both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and leeches on the two ankles; and leeching treats not blood, except for small impurities that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and therefore one does not weaken it much, as one does with purging of impurity;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it's not good that it be administered, nor with all heat nor without heat, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity of diseases or for custom, it's necessary to leech, let us administer each one hour in the beginning or end of the month, and at each time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are such people who, when they have need to leech, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are such people who find repletion and redness in their face, and on their head, and neck, and darkening of the eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such people who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and bleed gums.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such people who dream, and see by night blood and hurt and bites and seeming things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and likewise when it's in the middle of the month, let us order them to leech after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The purging of the mouth helps against the goutiness of the head... that comes to them, and it's not good that this be after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this leeching is in place of the purging of the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it's not good that those who are of cold complexion use it, or who have a catarrh, for this does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and therefore it's not good that the elderly use it, nor those who have cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who purify themselves with it often become forgetful, and because of this it's good to place the leech a little lower by the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Leeching in the neck is in place of purging the head and the bile, and because of this it's good for the constriction of the stomach.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for bursting of the channel of the womb, and for hiccough, and for repletion;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it's good to place [the leech] a little more deeply, because if it holds too tightly, it causes forgetfulness or stomach upset and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Leeching on the two sides of the neck is good for headaches, and eye pain and migraine, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it's in place of purging the bile; and let you command the leecher to express his hand before putting him [the leech], that he not strike the artery and cause excessive bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Leeching under the chin is good for mouth disease, and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it's in place of purging the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Leeching on the shoulders is good for disease that comes from heat and repletion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	Leeching on the sides [of the body] is as effective as purging the three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these thick veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the leecher that he not place him [the leech] too deeply, because the flesh is bare there and the nerves and arteries are underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech that is on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids of the fundament and for diseases underneath; and it's necessary that the leech be large and made of iron, so that it can bleed well; and if it were subtle, it would break through and make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leeches on the legs clearly purify, because they draw blood from all the body; and are good for old pains in the hips, and in the loins, and in the bladder, and dispel inflammation; and are in place of the two saphena veins, and the two ankle veins, and nonetheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause a feeling of lassitude in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the leech is to put it first empty, and let it suck immediately, and then place it hastily, and stir it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and appear the bloody juice; then take it off, and replace the leeches, and take note of the condition of the body, because there are some who have thick flesh, and clear pores: if so, it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a little deep, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it's necessary to prick two times: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it's necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, it's sufficient to do so only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, then we repeat often; and if the blood is thick, then prick deeply, and the end is that the heart be pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it's necessary for those who have thick skin and hard flesh, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the areas of the leeches with oil which is piercing and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it's in a state of being applied with oil of violets, or with the oil of sweet almonds, or with the oil of cucumber seeds.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it's in winter, with oil of chicory, or lily, or chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or oil of aniseed, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person who is being purged has tender flesh and large pores, then it's not necessary to apply any oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but rather to wash afterwards with red water, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who are very moist, should get up from the bed and wash with myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should get up from old wine, or water of sycamore, or a decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or other similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it's not necessary to purify with a leech before bathing in water or in a bath, but rather an hour or two after the bath; and do not sleep after the purging.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it's necessary that he wash himself when he is to be leeched and after being leeched.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who purge are choleric, and whose blood is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	for it's necessary that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in the morning, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink vinegar potions, and meat broth, and damp meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion should take honey syrup, and aromatic wine of moderate age, which is between old and new, and drink broth little by little, and drink vinegar potions and small birds, and chicken.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day that they are to be leeched, they should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it's necessary to give some men some trickele or muskete before the purging, or after, to comfort the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and be careful with the blood, but it's not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The leeches that are not put to prick are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the belly and the navel and the hips and the back, because those members do not bear being pricked there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and this is done only to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as when we put them on the shoulders when they are purging to remove the viscosity that is in the member, just as we put leeches on the belly and navel to reduce the member.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes pain when there is inflammation or swelling, and by its attractive virtue, it may possibly break the inflammation, or bring back the bone to its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and thus it does when one puts it on the liver and spleen when there is retained purulence.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these leeches are administered empty in order to suck only, and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of hot water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in cases of pleurisy, and in such a way that one fills the leech with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for this have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the leech administered at fire is:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has 2 inches of width and half a palm in depth, and on the side closest to the middle it has one small perforation, just like for placing an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it is made of iron, soft before so that it doesn't hurt the sick person when placed on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and in the middle a rod of iron or iron wire to place a candle enclosed.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they are made in great and small sizes according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the leeches of children are different from those of adults, and those of thin people are different from those of fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And so one should put this leech on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	take the candle made of wax or a linen strip, and put it in the leech through the rod that is inside the leech.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the leech so that it doesn't burn the sick person.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and be sure that the tube is over the perforation that we said about earlier, so that when you want to, you can let out the vapor, and take off the leech.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and then place a new linen strip as before, and repeat the process often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the leech administered in case of pleurisy, everything is water, there is no rod or perforation, and it's not administered with fire except when it's full of water, and it's placed on the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Leeches are not administered with fire except in members where one cannot put leeches for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare places of flesh, such as the neck and navel, and others similar.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find leeches in sweet and clean water without any impurity, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them into fresh water until they are fat and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then be purged with wine and leeches, and rub the member until it is red, and put on the leeches.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and have a pleasant smell, then it's the place where one can put a leech, then put them there, because this is very effective afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, lift the area up with a cloth and then with water, completely clean it, and then apply a poultice.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the area purifies too quickly in the body of the leeches, moisten a linen cloth with cold water and put it on, until the blood is cooled.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood is abundant, apply vitriol (a type of sulfuric acid) crushed or powdered, or galls, and similar things, until it is cooled.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half a handful of peeled peas on the area and let them sit until they have stopped bleeding, then it will now be staunched.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the leeches do not want to take hold, rub the area with fresh blood or prick it with a needle until the leech releases its grip.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach themselves.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are finished, sprinkle a little powder of aloes and burnt silk, or ashes on them, so that they will now become pleasant.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	And here begins the book of cuts (or wounds).
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a treatment for cuts and ulcers.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Pay attention, dear son, that the foolish men will fall from this chapter, for they have never read or seen any of the ancient books, nor have they learned anything.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is medicine estranged from our land, for I have never found a good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I don't know anything else except through the knowledge of ancient books, which I have studied so much that I've made it a part of my own learning, and through experience, and through the habituation of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have summarized it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters preceding these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us say the prologue of this book, which contains the summary of the words and chapters where the wise man puts his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who have been proven to be wise can know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when any person suffers a cut or dislocation or twisting or crushing, you should hasten to cure the sick person on both sides, and do not wait for anything else, such as weakness of body, or pregnancy, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the blood is too cold or too hot; and administer cold potions, that is to say, cooling drinks, and meat broth of lamb and goat, and do not drink wine, nor any greasy food, and do not fill him with rich meats that fill the vessels with blood, until you have no doubt about a warm putrefaction or spreading of matter in the member; but bring the sick person back to their first good governance as they had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that you feed the patient with meats that make great nourishing, or have viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and cheese, and peas, and veal, and fish fresh, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with great nourishment, the muscles repair themselves more quickly and the break heals sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old people and the decrepit do not heal well again nor knit together according to their nature due to the dryness of the members, nor those also who are too soft, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but rather scrape over the broken bone with a rough sponge that is hard and join the member together again, until it strengthens itself as it was before; and do not remove its work, and for this reason it is necessary to nourish it with rich meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the head is different from the break of the thigh or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that split into a splinter, and others that cut in a sliver, such as the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a break with an open wound, and a break with a small crack throughout.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each manner has its own method and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the memory recalls as being necessary.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the break of the bone is by the fact that the place is twisted and well open at the back, and resonates when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and if there is no twisting or resonance in the toucher, and the patient does not feel great pain, then it is not a break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can also have twisting, a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It's not necessary that you move the limb with your hand, but put on medications that come next, and then constrain it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that splits into splinters and are the two parts disjointed, you should now put them in a straight line, so that warm putrefactions do not occur.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if warm putrefactions come, let it alone for a day, until the putrefaction is calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then put it back in its original place, so that the muscles are lightly and gently touching each other, and know that the restoration of a single bone is easier than the restoration of one with fragments; then constrain it, as is necessary next.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone has fragments broken off in it, and there are two parts to them, whether they are hands or feet, or at your hand they are small members, or on two strings, or on one string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the limb back in its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are freed, scrape away with all tools the additions to their places at the muscles you touch, and take care that through your work, no harm or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you should be able to feel it with your hand if it doesn't seem right: straighten it well, and don't strain it too much, nor press it as those who bring about warm putrefaction and contraction in the member do, as we have often wanted.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is in place, instruct the patient to keep it still so it does not move, neither while sleeping nor waking, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take good care that the member is so secure that the patient feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it's not in place, and you must put it in such a condition that it doesn't feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is placed correctly, so that no twisting occurs when it's put back in place;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is according to what I'm telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in size, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar parts; they need to be wrapped in soft and subtle linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are big, such as thighs and legs: they need to be wrapped in a thick and sturdy linen cloth, for the large cloths encircle the whole great member and bind it from all sides equally, so that there is no sagging.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie around the ends of the lighter cloths, 3 turns or 4, according to the member, and bind your hand a knot in the whole cloth, then go above the break and bind it less tightly, so that the break is separated from the binding by a bit.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the cloth a bit and a bit more, until you take hold of a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another cloth and wrap it around again on top of the broken area.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break and bind it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first layer above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the cloths strips of linen or cloth, as long as it is all equal, then tie everything up with one bandage, and then put on top your well-made pads, if there's no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is a swelling or abscess, then put on top something soothing and hot that will draw out the abscess, and leave it thus for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind over your pads, and they should be of the thickness of a well-worn cane, or of wood from which one makes walking sticks, or of palm leaves, and they should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the pad which one puts on top of the break is a bit thicker and larger than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as it fits to the limb, whether big or small.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind on top of the pads in the same way that you did in the first layer, then tie over a string moderately, just like in the first layer over the break.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is on top, the less; and it is necessary that the string be moderate, neither too thick nor too thin, and be of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the string is too thick, it's like the works of fools who make their bandages with twisted linen threads, and that's a great mistake, because the bandage can't be even if it's too fine, and it shouldn't have more than two fingers' width between each pad.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the sick person is hurt by the scratches of the pads after being bound in their healthy areas, then put underneath them strips of linen or torn cloth to prevent it from bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is together with the break, and the skin is torn, I will say how to treat it later. (This seems to be a pause or a transition in the text, perhaps indicating that the description of the treatment for a specific type of injury is not yet complete.)
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it's not necessary to bind with pads all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it's not necessary to put on pads that are too tight before 5 or 7 days, or more according to your discretion in case of a hot abscess.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and see here the manner of ancient plasters to restore breaks, dislocations, and torsions: and it is that you take flour that is kept against the walls of a mill, and mix it with a great deal of egg, and put this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, on it, and use it; and it is the common manner of the plaster restoring breaks in many dispositions, and indeed for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring breaks, dislocations, and torsions: take 3 parts of barberry, danie (a type of plant), galbanum, asafoetida, and gum arabic, ana .x. Z.; myrrh and aloe, ana .v. Z.; aloes, 8 parts; and grind them into powder, and mix with a great deal of egg. If the complexion (color or temperament) of the person is hot, use this plaster, because it has good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is worth to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of plaster that is good for torsions: take mugwort and wormwood, ana .x. Z.; myrrh and aloes, ana .viiij. Z.; acacia, 6 parts; Armenian balm, .x. Z., and grind them well, then mix with water or a great deal of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of plaster for joints and bones that have been severed from their places, and calms the pain happening, and is used to cover the wound: take new linen, and soak it in warm water and oil, then put it on the place. This plaster does not restore, but it is good for calming hot abscesses, and properly removes pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of plaster that restores broken bones: take dry leaves of fig trees and leaves of wild pomegranate, and grind them together, then make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of plaster for the restoration of bone breaks and to ease the remaining pain from the abscess. Take roots of wormwood, camomile, flowers of violets, and flour of each one part; and grind them together, then mix with wine. And if the member is hot, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of plaster that is stronger than the first one, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the member. Take roots of wormwood, and seeds of flax, balaustine, melilotus, and marjoram, and flowers of violets and camomile, each one part; and grind them together, then mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates writes that when restoring a broken member, one should only put on it wax made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, and says that it should be between two (temperatures) neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that when restoring a broken member, one should put on it dry things that are slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is good for lesions and pain: take mugwort, the hair or wool of a depilated man (a person who has shaved their body hair), or bird's feathers, and wormwood, and equal parts, and grind them together, then make into a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen the plaster a little after, and be careful that the sick person does not feel any pain, nor has the bone come loose from its place; if so, do not remove the plaster for another day.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, or redness, or swelling, hurry and remove it, and take off the plaster now; and then take a light cloth and a damp sea sponge, and plunge them in water, and lift up the area, as long as the itching ceases and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, and then put on dry linen, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a cloth, as long as you are sure that there is no hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member rest and be gone, and the pain cease, then repeat the subtle binding and a little plaster, and do not bind it too tightly as before; and continue in this subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess, redness, pain, and swelling have all been removed, and you still need to use plaster and bandage, then repeat it, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if none of the things we have said come to the member, then do not remove it until after 3 days, or 4 days, or 5 days, or 7 days; and never leave it for more than 20 days, according to what you see, as long as the break is healing and approaching the joining of the flesh on itself.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then the wound will become more swollen and fleshy than before, as I said earlier. And if you see that the area is drying out more than necessary, know that necrosis cannot come to it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then take the cloth soaked in hot water and rinse it, every time you remove it, and do this three times a day, and let the bandage dry out a little.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work, the necrosis is cut off from the member, and it heals quickly what the foolish doctors have done by restoring the broken member in a wrong way: it's bad, and it's a cowardly craft, and I see nothing else but to let go and do things properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Il semble que nous avons terminé la discussion sur les plâtres et la restauration des os brisés.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaks, and diverse forms, and the causes are designated;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are breaks that are made by a blow from a sword, and the humerus breaks all the bone up to the shaft which is under the bone, as happens with a hatchet or axe; and for this reason this kind of break is called "hatchet break".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone above without piercing it, and this kind of break is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two breaks is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is a closed blow, or splitting, or a stone hammer, or falling on a stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is an impinging break, which approaches just to the membrane that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is closed up in the bone as subtly as a thread, and this break is small, and for this reason it is called "capillary break";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by being struck with a stone, or falling, or similar thing, and makes the piece of bone go inwards, and it leaves a hole that is like those made by cauldrons when they are heated over them; if the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in skulls that have soft bones, such as those of infants;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it happens with all these kinds of breaks in which small pieces are separated, such as those; and I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of breaks by the signs on them, and by the investigation made, and by the corrupted flesh that is on them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary break is recognized by this: when the bone has been uncovered and you rub your finger over it, if the break appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, be careful for the bad accidents that come to the patient, and if you see any evil accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and swelling, and bruising, and high fever, and the skin is hot and red, and other similar symptoms in different dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any evil accident, and you hope for healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes first to you, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone in front of the 14th day at most that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, so that the membrane under the bone does not become corrupted, and the accidents we have spoken of come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break in the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to split the broken part thus: and this is to take hold of the head of the wounded patient, and uncover over the bone in all ways that you can, and on the surface of the wound more gently than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if a bloody discharge comes to uncover the bone, or an ugly boil forms, then it needs the help of what is necessary, and this is that you fill the place with damp cloth soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and make the wound rest as long as the ugly boil is calmed down, and you are sure of the stopping of the bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove it, and this is done in two ways of operation: one way is that you cut from the narrow part in front, and this shape is:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another swelling larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various swellings, some are high and others wide, and they are sharp-edged, and of iron hardness; and work on them lightly, so as not to bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, so that you administer swellings with awls, but not so deeply that they do penetrate outside the skullbone, and there should be a margin or a circle above the point, so as not to let the point pass beyond the bone; and you will need several, so that each one comes into place on the edge of the bone, so that you have awls for all skulls; and this is the shape of the three ways of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one awl on the bone and turn it back to your hand so long as you know that the bone is pierced; then place the awl elsewhere a little bit later, and do this all around, then file with the edges of the bones which are between the perforations, and make it finer than you can, and lightly, just as we have said, so that you draw the bone to your hand or to any of the instruments that you have such as pliers, pincers; and be sure not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and filed the bone, it is necessary that you sharpen the remaining part of the bone to every single other instrument resembling an awl, but it should be sharper and finer than the other awl.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains nothing of the small bones or scales, lightly scrape them off with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with threads and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of doing it is that which Galen says, who is very wise; and I speak very strongly about it, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You need to describe the process of treating a certain type of injury.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut off one part, and the part is in two edges, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet upwards, so that you lightly scrape around the entire bone, and take good care to avoid the membrane below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is scraped against the bone, then lightly scrape around, because you must scrape very little harm and with no danger.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breakage does not penetrate all the way to the membrane, and the bone is scraped so only above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to cover that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you must have different quantities of, in order to adjust according to the work and figure of the breakage.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you scrape with large rasps first, and then with finer ones, and do not cease to do so until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other fine cutters and subtle breakages, it is necessary that you adjust according to its direction; and this is something that is not answered by him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, then it is necessary that you take one cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and place it over the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another doubled cloth in two or three layers, and wet it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so that you do not irritate the wound, then apply over it one other linen, and do not tighten it too much so that it only covers the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And leave it like this for one or two days, until the suppurative (or pus-filled) part is calmed down, then remove it and apply medications such as lily roots, ground ivy flour, frankincense powder, aristolocha, and similar things; make a powder from these things and place it on the wound, and apply medicinal treatments without letting it become inflamed.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And take care that the wound is completely clean, so as not to leave any ointment or let it form a scab, for when a scab forms over the brain tissue, it runs and spreads, causing great harm to the patient. For when something caustic (or acid) is applied to the wound, it burns above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any evil accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if the evil comes from no other cause than the medicine that you have put on it, as great virtue as it has, then it is necessary for you to take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them together in one cloth, and apply this to the sore.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it in the ways of treatments that are necessary until it is healed.
