Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken or one separately, for they are two bones; and the part below is cartilaginous, and does not break, so it heals without being further inflamed or twisted.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should straighten your little nose or nostril, and put this break inside into your index finger, and then push it forward, until the nose returns to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and take heed that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and it cannot be brought back into place, then you should put it on top of a small reed, a little bit large.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in both parts, then do it in the same way, and hasten to restore it at first light, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling has subsided, then straighten it at the tip of the nose with a cloth of linen, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you straighten it from the other side, if the break is there; and let the strips be so thick that they fill up the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some restorers say that the strips should be moistened with lard and changed every day. It doesn't seem good to me, but it's necessary that they are moistened in a mixture of wheat flour, egg whites, and miller's powder; then leave the strip, as long as the bone is firm and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes they bind on or to the nose a feather from a goose in place of strips, and if it has a soft drape that keeps the break in place, and blows gently through it, then do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the swelling comes to the nose while you are working on it, then put in a plug of cerate or moistened cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a little bit of dragon's blood.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the swelling doesn't come, then put an ointment on the outside, made with sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, and put on some light bandages, but don't bind up the nose.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break of the nose is small and it's broken into little pieces, then bring them to suitable instruments for this purpose, then sew up the crack, and mend with things that dissolve and bond like pastes and ointments suitable for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there's no wound inside the nose, then sew it up with threads and put in catgut strings, until it's healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the distortion of the jawbone.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is distorted downward and there is no external wound or break, and the break is only visible from the inside, so that it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the break is in the right part, that you place your index finger inside the patient's mouth; and if the break is on the left side of the jawbone, then place your index finger from the right hand, and press the break inside slightly, and then hold it with the other hand outside and straighten.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jawbone is separated in three parts, it is necessary that you administer an extension of three parts, as long as it becomes straight.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth have caused displacement or distortion, tie one end of a thread of gold or silver or silk to each tooth, then place on the broken jaw salve and on top of it a double cloth; and on top of the cloth a well-made bandage or a piece of leather the same size as the jaw, long and wide, and tie it above the mouth that you can breathe, and command the patient to rest and take light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the face is changing, untie it on the third day, and then reapply what has changed; and apply a poultice with flour powder mixed with egg or fine wheat flour after removing the salve; and put a light linen cloth over it. If the poultice hardens and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until they are healed, as many people have been healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses or swelling occur, administer what we have said before many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, treat the exposed piece of bone as dead, that is, do not take it as living tissue; rather be careful to remove it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it gradually with flames according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the pieces [of the cautery], and there is no longer any of it remaining, if the wound is large, apply one of the ointments that are suitable for this, to dry out pus, until it heals.
de la forcele	with forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps broke several times in front of the shoulder, and the break is three different ways: either it is broken and split into two, with pieces, and this is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with an open wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is this: when there is no open wound with the break, you should have two assistants, one of whom will hold the broken forceps in place; and the other will straighten out the arm towards the affected area. Then insert both ends of the break into your hands, so that it takes shape as it should, and there is neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch it further, place under the patient's shoulder a rounded stick of cloth or linen, and as thick as necessary; then extend and hold the forceps, and strain the stick in your hand, so that you insert both ends of the break into place as they should.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you can't pull the head of the forceps out to the front because it's coming out from behind, then it's necessary for the patient to lie on their side and place a pillow under their shoulder; and have the assistants push down on the patient's shoulder, so that the bone of the forceps is elevated.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then bring the break to your hands, and if you find it is not properly aligned, it's necessary for you to split it open; and pull out the pieces lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined together in any way, then cut it with one of the clippers that you have; but place the instrument under the forceps to protect the joint.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And make a spoon shape, and it should not be convex, and it should be as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two handles, as you see fit, with one being wide and the other narrow, similar to the outline of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure that the abscess is hot, then cauterize the wound; and if the scab is small or you doubt whether it's a hot abscess, then fill the wound with linen and thread, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then soak a piece of linen in rose oil and onion juice and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, is that you place on the bone a plaster made from miller's flour and egg white, and put on light bandages, and place a stick under the saddle, if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very thick bandage of a palm in width, then put one double fold on top of the straps, and the filler; then take a thin needle of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandaged part, so that the chief end of the bandage is hanging.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and put the needle on top of the breakage, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy saddle, and under the sick saddle; and sew it in each part, and when you see that the stitch holds the breakage properly, and you see clearly that the needle does not move above the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the stitches loosen, then hold it back.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the sick person sit on their back, and he puts a small bolster under the saddle, so that it lifts the aid in high; thus it will lighten the break of the shoulder by the alignment of the arm with the neck, or you tie the arm to the collar, and do not untie it for bad incidents to come, until twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then start the filler again if you see that it is necessary, and tighten it and leave it so until he is restored; and it is restored in the best way in twenty-eight days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	The shoulder break.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the shoulder breaks or is severely dislocated from its place and you cannot see that it has been hurt by force, if it appears according to the figure of the breakage, and you reset it according to its natural shape in all ways that you can; then put on the place powder made from a mill with an abundance of egg whites and light stitches, and put over .i. (one) double cloth; then put over a wide and subtle bandage, one pace larger than the shoulder, and sew ribbons under it at any place on the shoulder, so that you tie that ribbon of linen threads, so that the bandage lies evenly; and then bind it tightly with a great strap so that the bandage does not move from its place, and look after the patient each day; and every time he becomes sore, bind him again, put the bandage back even if it is out of its place, and lay the sick person on his side. And the shoulder will be restored in twenty days or twenty-five.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone projects forward and touches under the skin, then make a cut up to it and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the boil to calm hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the boil
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The boil is sometimes broken inside, but that does not often happen; but it breaks out to the outside. And when it is broken inwards, it subsides under, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of appetite, and fever, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens up the sinews in the broken bone, and it feels quite well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and puts a pillow between their shoulders, then presses their shoulders, and gathers together the ribs of the two broken ribs with one's hands, and subtly makes it even in every way that you can, until the shape of the bone is such as it should be; then puts poultices and bandages on top of the sterile cloth of salt, or another light wood, and wraps it up in one piece of cloth, and ties it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turns the tie around to the back, and tightens it gently, and rewards each hour with a loosening, and if it becomes too loose, then tightens it; and if it needs to be untied because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten and untie it, and scrape off the poultice, and address what has come there in ways of cures; then scrapes off the poultice, and tightens until it is sound.
de la brisure des costes	It seems like you're referencing a medieval medical text!
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not come from anywhere other than large bones behind the back, and within the head, and they do not bend outward only because they are slippery; and people sense this well when examining the vertebrae.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the remedy is that you put back in place the breakage, just as it should be. And then apply a poultice and bind with an iron band if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib breakage is bent inward, the patient feels very great pain and puncture, as well as a sense of being pierced, because the bone pierces the flesh; and they feel sharp pains, are hot and vomit large quantities of blood, and this is a grave condition, and the ancients have devised great remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that inflate the belly, so as to drive the breakage outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot swellings come from it, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then let them heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us said that one should apply cupping glasses on the spot to draw out pus strongly, and this seems like a good idea; however, there is doubt whether the cupping glass might attract unwanted fluids to the spot due to the weakness of its constitution.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of us said that the spot should be covered with wet wool soaked in hot oil, and a poultice placed between the ribs to put the warmth all around it, then it should be treated as one would treat pleurisy, with meat and medicines.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain because of the bone piercing the flesh, and is in doubt, it is necessary to make an incision above the broken rib and place an instrument underneath to protect the viscera; then one must cut the bone and draw it out lightly, and afterwards sew shut the two lips of the wound, if they are large, and treat with poultices until he is healed. And if a hot swelling comes, one should place wet compresses soaked in rose oil on top of the area; and cure the area with these poultices for as long as it takes to get rid of the swelling, and be careful not to disturb the viscera that are there, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	It seems like you've jumped back to a new topic! "De la brisure du col" means "Of the breakage of the neck". Would you like me to help with something specific related to that?
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	None are born with a breakage of the neckbone and they become crippled because of it; and similarly to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And if it happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, take note of whether their hands are soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, if there is no feeling, then know that they are mortal in many dispositions. But if they can move and feel well when you press on them and prick them, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if you apply treatment to it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will be healed or not, take note if the feet are softened, and if the accidents that occur in the hands are like those that happen in the back, and there is vomiting and diarrhea without any effort; and when one has relieved themselves on their stomach, if they still have diarrhea without any effort. And when it is relieved on its back and they want to sit up, if they cannot, know that it is mortal: do not bother with its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come upon them, then the thing will be much lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply if there is a hot swelling: place on the spine rose oil or oil of mustard egg, until it is calmed down. Then place on one of the soothing and drying poultices, and bind with a cloth, and command the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the part where they feel the pain, until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones become separated, you must cover the area with a dressing; and remove the bone, then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture. Then treat with ointment from fresh meat, until it is healed. And if the joint of the bone is broken, which is called the "joint of the knee", take your purse in your left hand and place it equally to the other hand at your power; then apply the poultice and splint over it, if you need them; then tighten the splint, and if there are any loose bones, make them secure, and remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.

de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", where one is small, and that is the one that touches the shoulder; and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the small joint; perhaps only the large bone is broken, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is broken, the restorations are easy, and the healings; and when the large one is broken, it is a poor healing, and more painful than when both together are broken. If it's only the small bone that is broken, then the point of the elbow should be slightly extended, and kept straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large bone, then it needs to be strained more strongly; and it should be stretched up on one cushion, and the elbow of the patient should be kept higher than usual, and the small joint lower than usual, and the patient should be crossed over himself, with a cushion in front of him higher than his own body, so that the patient does not suffer any pain. Then the attendants' hands should be extended to the part below the patient's hand, or to one of the joints, and another attendant to the other side above. And then the patient should be made to relax evenly, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break has pieces, then put each in its place, and if there is one that is loose, grab it quickly, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we said before, and sew up the skin, with a thread of the same kind.

Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the treatment a suppurating abscess appears, then apply one cloth made from rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard or too soft; and tie the cloth gently on top so that the abscess is calmed. And then remove the ointment and put the poultice of miller's powder with a lot of egg whites on it, then place the stars (straps or bandages), and let the star over the fracture be stronger and slightly larger than the others; and know that there should be 6-7 stars or more depending on the situation: whether the break is in one bone or two. And strain the plaster more strongly over the break, but not too loose, as I said at the beginning of this chapter. And let the cloths above the break be soft and moist, and not hard or harsh; and let the strings (by which it's strained) be made from linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And if any bad accident happens to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you should soak the member in hot water until the itch is calmed; and let the member not rest too tightly. Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too narrow, then you must soften it with one part of vinegar and let it be for some days, until the swelling flows into it, and then bind.
