de la brisure de la main	of the dislocation of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand there are two places where many times dislocations occur, and there does not come but a fold.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the wrist of the hand is dislocated or folded, it is necessary that the patient cross his legs and sit straight in front of him equally; then he puts his hand on the table extended, and extends the fingers of the broken bones, and makes them equal with a ruler, until they are well joined; and he applies an ointment and bandages, if swelling comes, then he puts an iron splint according to the quantity of the bone; and it is wrapped in one cloth of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the dislocation is around the fold of the wrist, he makes a sphere with cloth, and commands the patient to apply it to his broken wrist; and then binds it with a long cloth, and let the iron splint be as soft as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as it is necessary.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the dislocation is on the outside, it is necessary that you put an iron splint above, and another below in the wrist, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind the whole hand together, and tighten the string between the two bones.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the dislocation occurs in any of the two bones, and it is a luxation, you should make them equal, as necessary; and bind with the wrist, and if you see that you put a small straight iron splint to lift the dislocation, and do not move; and if the dislocation is on other bones, such as in the index or one of the others, you should make them equal, and tie with the healthy bone that comes after; or tie them all together in one bandage, whichever is more useful; or put a splint above, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken bladder (or possibly "broken crucible" given the context of medieval medical practices)
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the bladder are often broken, and well does one see this when it turns before and behind; and the restoration is such that one ties a cord above the breakage, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then stretches out each of his servants with their cord to his equal part, and this is when the breakage is in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the breakage is close to the root of the bladder, then one of the cords should be directed towards the groin, and the other cord below the breakage. And similarly if it is close to the knee, then the cord should be placed near the knee, and the extension downwards; then place the splint alongside the bone in both hands, so that it is according to its natural shape, and then put the plaster, and tie it, lest there come a swelling in it.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot swelling, let it calm down then return to your work and treatment; the bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It's necessary that you wrap a strong double bandage in 2 or 3 layers over the breakage, and let the superfluous parts remain; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and insert a long thread between the bladder and the leg, near the knee below, and have the end of the thread come up; then wrap the bandage on top of the leg and on top of the bladder, then place stars on the breakage, and put a star on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the bladder with soft cloth to equalize the pressure; then begin to tie tightly 3 or 4 turns around the breakage; and as you go up from the breakage, the constriction will be less; then take the two ends of the thread that you have inserted between the leg and the bladder, and tie three stars on top, then go back down to the bottom of the thread, until you reach near the foot; and if it remains in its place, without moving, then let it stay like that, lest there come a swelling, inflammation or any other appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it starts to come undone, then untie it and address the problem as we have said many times before. And if there are fragments of bone that get in the way, it is necessary to remove them, if possible; and if not possible, it is necessary to cut the affected area and extract the fragments; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And at any time the joint is broken in such a way that stars are placed within it, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration made in this manner the patient's joints do not creak.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the joint is restored within one day or slightly less or slightly more, according to the diversity of temperaments.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the knee joint there is little breakage, but it folds many times. And if it breaks, then it is just one crack or one hole, and it has to be stitched, and when stitched, it feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts back what was torn to its place, as long as it can be assembled; then apply the plaster and put an iron band around it, if necessary, and tighten it so as it should be; then reward all the preparations that we have said for other breaks, such as applying hot poultice and similar remedies; and put on each accident what is needed, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called the "tibia" (mustelz) and the other the "fibula" (foscile); and it has the same kind of breakage as it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is the same as that of the arm; and the works are all alike.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns out of shape in every part.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the tibia (subtilz) bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the fibula (gros os) bone is broken, it feels like great pain and can be seen well; and it turns downwards. Then add a splint, and put it back in place, and tie the bandages equally; but however, it's necessary to see if the break is ugly and there are multiple pieces, that the splint be shorter and lighter; and loosen according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two strips of wood that are curved to fit the leg on one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee to the ankle. Then wrap them in two loops, one above and one below, and tie a bandage around them in the middle. And at this point, the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and that is good. Some also give a wooden splint of the same length as the leg, made of wood, and place the leg on it to prevent movement, and properly dress the wound in the break where there was an injury. And move each day the leg, to see if there is hot swelling or another accident; and treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no breakage, but the bones of the foot sometimes break and become disjointed, and there are few cases that do not require a cast to immobilize them.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot and you see them protruding one over the other, place the sick foot on the ground, as if it were going to walk, then put your healthy foot on top of the sick one, where the bones are elevated. Then press down on the sick foot so that they return to their proper place. Next, apply a splint and bandages, and place a small wooden plate with two pegs under the belly of the foot. Tighten it firmly against the foot, then wrap drapery around it and do other things as needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four will have passed, then loosen the tie, for you will find the bones equalized, broken, or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the broken bones, then restore them, as we have said to do with the wrist of the hand. Then put a splint on the broken bone according to its length and let it be one piece more wide; and under the foot, that tablet which I have said, and strain it properly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, then place a splint over each bone according to its size, wrapped in one cloth of linen, and strain the tablet under the foot; and let it be so that the top of the tablet is outside the belly of the foot, so that it fits well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things which I have said about other fractures, when we have spoken of them; and support each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's pelvis is fractured, then make her sit up and enlarge it, then incline it towards the back part, and hold it in place; then fill the natural cavity with cotton, and insert as much as one fist; then drop the woman, and lift up the back little by little, and then the cotton will burst forth, so that it comes to the entrance of the nature, and returns the bone with the fist; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in place, and do this for about seven days or so: then the fracture will be restored; and if you see fit, take a bladder of vetches, and tie a string to the anus, and insert the whole bladder into the natural cavity; then blow into the string strongly, until the bladder is inflated inside: the nature will return to its place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it in that state for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the thumb of man or woman is fractured, then restore it in the same way that we have said for the hip; and do not hide these nearby fractures from him who puts his study and his skill into it, and listens to my book. For the fracture signifies the right path of restoration in many dispositions: listen then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose's girth and wrap the thigh in it; then envelop with linen cloth around, and leave for 3 days or wrapped around, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with wound, even if it is great, such as the thigh or arm bone, that he be healed now, so that the stitches which we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals and leaves a scar of vitriol, then if you have nothing else, then start to restore the break again in that same hour, or on that same day, lest suppuration does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if suppuration comes, then leave the restoration just for nine days, until the suppuration is calmed, and do not touch it nor in the third day nor on the quarter, because you would bring evil accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears on the surface above the skin uncovered, then it is necessary that you put it to slight point with your hands, with small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not prepared for you to put it in your hands, then take this instrument that is made of iron, which has 7 or 8 fingers long, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and because of this, it is necessary for the master to take 3 or 4 [of them], as needed for each treatment of a broken bone; and let it be round and thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the member at your work, and have a sharp point in front, and be thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", for which reason it is necessary that the curved nails be put on top of the visible bone; and push it once, until it comes back, and be equal one against the other. And if the break is subtle, and the instrument cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the tip of the bone, so that the instrument can get a good grip on it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone to its place, as we have said, then cut off what remains in the bone with a suitable instrument for this purpose, or with a knife or saw, according to your skill; then scrape out from the bone whatever is left of sharpness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is in its place and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position. Make sure it is in its correct place, then soak a cloth in strong black vinegar and properly clean the area; and do not put cerate or any other ointment on the wound, lest you cause suppuration and corruption to come; then administer these remedies as long as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted with the break; and many times this has been done by foolish doctors, and they have brought death or corruption upon the patient once. And the constriction is softer and more gentle than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that some evil accident may occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, then it is not necessary to put on poultices; but envelop the area around with hard cloths, and tie them. And when you see after one day or two that pus begins to form in the wound, then remove what you have put on top, and apply salving ointments for healing wounds, such as tetrafarmacian ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you stretch the member two times a day, morning and evening, until it is stitched and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be wrapped in such a way that the bow (or fold) goes down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it does not heal the next day, and it cannot heal but swells again, know that there are small bones inside, so you should probe the wound with a tent, and take out all those loose bones that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if an abscess or other kind of corruption comes to the place, you should treat it, according to what is written in its chapter above. And when the bone is broken and visible on the limb, like the bone of the thigh or the upper arm, and similar ones of the large limbs, do not pull it out, for many times death ensues, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out after 20 days or 30, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	the boils that come on the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They come often after the healing of the break, just when it's near the joint, and it is a sad thing to see the shape of the limb; and perhaps the member cannot do its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	So then be careful if the boil is fresh: if you apply medicinal compresses, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarsaparilla, aloe, and similar others, either taking one of these things or all together, and mixing them with astringent wine or egg white or oil; and putting it on the boil in bandages, tightly binding it, and not loosening it for many days; and then unbinding it, and doing another one, until the knot is removed; or straining it over a well-made linen cloth; because the property of the cloth is that it removes all swellings from the members. And if the knot has already become hardened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, you should cut into it above, and make its superfluity apparent; or have it cauterized by a surgeon, until it is removed, and then cure it as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break of the bone is restored, and the member remains weak and fragile after healing, it happens for many reasons: because one was bound too tightly, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and the swelling could not come to the member; or due to numerous abscesses; or due to excessive movement, not in its time; or because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you feed the sick person, and make their body soft, until there is an abundance of blood in them; and bathe them, and give them joy and happiness; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts a great swelling, and the abscess bursts with a clear pus, until the swelling comes to the member; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the deformed limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is still open, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that the limb should be broken all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and comes to great harm, and perhaps even death. However, if the swelling and pain are fresh, it is necessary to have them burst with hot water, or cooked soothing herbs, such as chamomile flowers, roots, and leaves, and similar things; and make a soft poultice, like well-made diacolin, and take the milky juice of chamomile, and mix it with chicken fat or sesame oil, and make a poultice on it; or take fatty figs, and crush them with colophon flax, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And at no time is it removed by constant and prolonged rubbing with wet hands, and the member should be moved each hour to restore its flexibility.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and strengthened like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, so that it needs to be cut just up to the bone, lightly and subtly at the incision; and apply cauterization and poultices in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the Book of Dislocations (or "Les Dislocations" in French)
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is from some joint out of its place, for which it cannot move, and the member is misshapen, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in anyone, then he must now bring back to its place carefully.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the place becomes inflamed, and by chance if it is put back in its place with pain; therefore it does not need to be moved until it is no longer inflamed: many times brings on spasms and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Nevertheless, when this happens, one must make the patient healthy again, then leave him until the swelling is reduced; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then rinse it lightly, and heal each member as the remedy comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have written down the chapters on dislocation from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Whatever happens when the jaws are dislocated and out of place, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are slightly moved from their place and become a little soft; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and drip saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return by itself within a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and fully formed, you should rinse it immediately, and not delay.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and in such a way that the servant will hold the patient's head, and insert one end of the mirror into the root of the dislocation in the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is on two sides; and with the other hand, push it back to put everything right again.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the mirror straightens it, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to put back into place, even if both jaws are together, then raise them with hot water and oil, until you lightly rinse them; do not delay in putting it back into place, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are put back in place and the patient's mouth closes tightly without any softness, then take damp cloths made of rose oil and wax, and lightly bind them around the patient's jaw.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient should sleep on their back, and their legs be placed between two cushions, so that they do not move to either side, nor try to mix their food, but take light food until the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then eat and drink as they wish lightly, and do not exert themselves to open their mouth to eat and drink, until the jaw is well healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not converted to their proper position, then fevers and sharp pains come, and possibly dysentery, and possibly vomiting of cold and pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these things, then know that it is a misfortune, and beware, for many times death comes to him who has this affliction within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the jawbone (or "mandible")
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The jawbone cannot descend from the side into the cavity of the mouth and back of the jaw, and it is descended only once outward, and one can easily feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back and stretches out their arms, then presses the place forcefully against your palm, and it will return, then apply the poultice and bandage to hold it in place.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the leg which is on the side cannot descend; if it does not stay down and comes up at all, then rinse it back into place, just as we have said. Then apply the poultice and bandage to hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and similarly the leg on the other side is also brought back into place when it has been pulled out of its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: first, when it slips down to the lower part of the arm; second, when it slips under the pit (or armpit); and third, sometimes it slips up, and these happen rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	and it does not dislocate backward for the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward for the nerves; but rather it dislocates downward towards the arm, just as in those who have too much flesh, for then it slips out quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it slips out slowly and comes back slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens that the shoulder of some men is bruised or crushed and becomes swollen with a hot pustule, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So you should inspect it thoroughly until you are certain, and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is evident that a shoulder dislocation occurs when the arm hangs down towards the waist, and you will notice a clear distinction between the healthy and diseased shoulders, and there will be obvious differences.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and you will find that there is a hollow or depression at the top of the diseased shoulder, and under the arm, right against the chest, it feels like an ox's fist; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move any part of their body.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it will not be hidden, because you can feel it clearly at the touch.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this type of dislocation is not easily to be reduced when it is new or if the infant is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the attendants lift the patient's hand up high, then place their fingers under the arm, and forcefully lift the joint back to its proper place; then the attendants lift the hand and extend it upwards, and put it in its place, and it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come back as we have said within two days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the attendants should apply a soothing and calming ointment, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and mealytle in water, and bring it to them.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then the patient should be wrapped up on their back, and a woolen pad is placed under the arm, not too soft nor too hard, then the attendant places their hand with the palm on top of the pad, and gently lifts the top of the shoulder, and pulls the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	and another attendant should press the top of the patient's shoulder so that it does not move downward; with this motion, the shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it reduces in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and you should have a man present who is larger than the patient, and standing at the side, and he should press his shoulder under the patient's arm, and lift the patient's arm up high, so that the patient hangs in it.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	and another attendant should pull the patient's hand down towards their stomach. And if the patient is too light, you can hang something heavy on them, and the dislocation will come back immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And the reduction can also be done in another way: and it is by placing a long wooden dowel in the ground, whose diameter is as wide as a fist, and not too thick or too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then it is placed under the patient, but with a soft cloth draped over it, and the patient's leg is extended out from the long dowel, then their hand is stretched down from the other side forcefully, and the joint will return to its proper place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if it still doesn't want to return despite all the things we've said, then do this cure: take a dowel of two arms in length and three thumbs in width, with a pointed end that can easily enter deep into the armpit, shaped as follows:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the patient's head on the top of a staff or pole, so that the staff does not hurt the patient; then place the support under the patient; and extend the arm over the long rod, and tie the shoulder to the rod, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm on one side of a sling made from an ash tree of wide branches, and let the hands be extended downwards, and let the body hang down from the other side: the joint will now return.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is set, in whatever manner, it is advisable that you put under the support a spire of wool equal in size; then apply the poultice around the powder from the mill, with incense and egg white, on all the shoulder and around, then place the strap under the support gently, and turn the string over the poultice, and encircle the hand around his neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is advisable that he rest a little while, until the members are comforted, for it will heal faster; and then rest a bit more after five or seven days, and move him; and if it is firm and has not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is inflamed from being too hot or wet as it came in, or for another reason, it is advisable that you administer cauterization on three holes, just as they are placed before a cauterizer's instrument (chapître).
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it breaks apart after seven days, and the joint does not hold together, and cannot lift his arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is torn, stretched or loosened; and know that the joint will never be mended in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The displacement that occurs near the chest, shoulders, or back is caused by sudden impact and stretching of the hands, and it is administered in another manner; and treat until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there is inflammation in the member, and slow movement, then the patient should bathe many times until that inflammation is alleviated, and it returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	the cost of a dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the dislocation of a joint is inflamed to points, and returns to points; and it is inflamed from all sides, and indeed in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reset, for one can see it well and feel it well; and is inflamed according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you put the diseased joint together with the healthy one, if it's visible clearly. For the joint is swollen, and cannot flex the arm, nor reach its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it's necessary that you clean it out while the swelling comes to its peak, for if the swelling comes to its peak, it would be painful to bring it back; and by chance it may not be able to be brought back in full, especially when it is at the back; this one is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and by chance death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that you can bring it back, that you stretch out its hand with your two hands; and its arm is extended, and the fingers of the doctor around the joint, above and below, and press the joint into its proper place, where it returns to its natural position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will return when he doubles his hand to his other hand, and presses the joint that is swollen at its root in the palm.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it doesn't want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and it is that two ministers stretch out the arm, and hold it tight with both hands, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from one side to the other, once you have wrapped a double, long, and wide bandage around it.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when the doctor has joined the joint to his hand, he will apply some oil there to soften the joint, then press the joint firmly, so that it returns to its place.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is back in place, he will put on dry poultice with an egg yolk, and bind the arm to the neck of the patient, and let it stay for some days, then remove the binding.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, he will remove the binding and let it be; and if you see that the joint doesn't hold well, he will reapply the poultice and the bandage, and leave it like this for some days, until it's firmly set; then he will remove the bandage.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain or discomfort after the joint has been put back in place, and it starts to swell again, he will bathe and rub it gently, and press on it until it's relieved. Or you put a fat lamb's poultice on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let it go into the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when he sweats, he will rub the joint gently, then put the poultice back on, and then put him into the bath; and do it this way two or three times until he's healed. And if you see that it still doesn't improve, he will put on warm moistened flax with butter, and bind it on; it will return to its natural state.
li dislocation de la main	It seems we've reached the end of this medical text! The author appears to have been describing various treatments for joint dislocations, specifically focusing on the hand.
