Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is swollen, and the return to its place is light, more than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place quickly, even if it is swollen or a warm abscess has formed there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the reduction is such that you place the ailing hand on a table, and extend the fingers of the other hand, and the mirror [or reflecting surface] place equal, thus that he puts his palm on the appearance of the jointure, and press it so that it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	However, it is necessary that you see if it is well in place; then put the ailing hand's back on a table at extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then put the ailing person's back of their hand on the table, and the mirror place its hand on that appearance of the jointure. If it returns now, it's well.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, then apply a strain of soothing plasters over the boil, and leave it thus without re-starting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it in place after some days, then the twisted jointure will remain.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and do nothing to harm the ailing person except until their hand is mollified and cannot strain anything at all: then know that the nerves are crushed, or the arteries; if there is no other remedy besides straining through cautery near the case, and perhaps it is worth nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, then put on the plaster that we have said, then strain and leave it for 5 days, then unbind and let it be so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then soak it in hot water, and rub it until it is clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	The text appears to be a medieval medical treatment for a specific condition, likely a shoulder or elbow dislocation, given the mention of the "dos de la main" (back of the hand) and the instructions on how to treat it. The text seems to be written in Middle French, which was the language spoken in France during the medieval period.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	At any time are dislocated the two bones of the hand on each side, sometimes to the back of the palm or to the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then the two bones are aligned and you push the dislocation to your fingers as long as it comes back, then support the head of the two bones, and push it towards the part where it is disconnected.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	and let it alone for two days, and then put it in place that day; and of necessity you must bind it, as we have said, and the dislocation of the day, and make it moveable, and reattach it to the nut; and do this often, until it is tight.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same thing if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand, and do just what you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same thing also, when it is dislocated from the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the shinbone of the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shinbone of the back or of the knee is dislocated, or there are more than one dislocations, then there is no cure, because the bone hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the excretions jump out without will, nor can they hold them, and many times are softened any member, or both hips or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the shinbone moves to four parts; that which moves at the back is called "giltboziture" (or possibly "giltbozitz"), and another part seems to move in a way that it can't be described...
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment is as follows, if the swelling has come from childhood: there will be no cure or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And the one that comes from falling or blows or similar things, as the old people said, it is not a great benefit in all cases.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that occurs in front of the knee, there is no cure or healing.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also that which occurs directly in the two sides, and one cannot cure it except for that which comes to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the sick person's face should be spread evenly over one level and have a strain underneath him so he does not bleed.
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then stick one ember at the head in the earth firmly, and another near the feet, and tie a linen strip behind the sick person's thighs, and also around their hips, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two attendants know the linen strips, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two embers.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well closed, the ember as we have said, and the patient should put their hands on the spine firmly, until it revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it doesn't revive with this treatment, take a board three arm-lengths long, and hollow out the middle of it, and the patient should be on their side, and put the head end of the board under their back, then place the middle part of the board over the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and have the patient put their feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until they revive again to the same level; and if you see fit, do it in a turner which turns to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And it is that you stick two embers at the head of the sick person, one arm-length apart, and near the feet, two others, and have between each ember, above and below, a palm's length of space.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and have in each ember one hole, or the turner's core, and let the embers be firmly stuck in the earth, so they don't move; and between each pair of embers there should be one turning ember, on top of which the linen strip turns, and in each turning ember there are two small embers an inch long, to turn the turner.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the linen strip that is between the thighs to the turner near the head, and the other linen strip near the feet to the other turner, and each of the attendants turns their turner to tighten the entire linen strip, and the master puts the spine even as we said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it's evened out, he puts on a drying plaster with plenty of egg, and then the dressings, and then the splint from a board three finger-breadths long, which will support the level of the swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a linen strip, as we said, and use subtle nourishment for the sick person until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if nothing comes to an end with the healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the splint that we have said before; and at no time should one administer a piece of cloth.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and if any appearance comes in the back part of the spine of the back, and it seems like dislocation; and it's the bone that has opened up, so one should not have any assumption: perhaps death would come from it.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is said that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only through dislocation, and it does not come to them as with other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside there is less displacement before and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and it opens up more the sick knee than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the hollow that is near to a swollen and hot apostume because the veins of the thigh come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him whose it comes outside, is that this accident is contrary to those in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him whose it comes to the front, is that his leg seems well according to the completion; however, he does not double his knee without pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and retains his urine, and swells the groin, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him whose it comes to the back, is that he cannot straighten his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and the veins of the thigh are at the hollow under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation is that you return to see if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its disposition, there is no cure for it; and there is no need to have any expectation.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that where the dislocation is fresh, and it's of four kinds of dislocation, you hasten to turn back the joint, both inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will come back, and there's no need for further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it doesn't come back in this way, you need to call for one strong surgeon, and hold the leg very tight with two hands, or one ligature tied above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another surgeon stretches his hand up in such a way that he puts his hands under his buttocks, then tightens the ligature with one smooth pull above the thigh; and another ties the head of the ligature.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they stretch upwards and downwards all at once, so that the sick person is lifted from the ground all at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to three kinds of dislocations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it's good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not, it is necessary to apply a cure to its appearance. When the dislocation is in the shoulder area, it is necessary that you bind the patient on his healthy side, then put the strap on the root of the scapula, and the place under the angle, then tighten the strap up towards the angle, and towards the forceps;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take other attendants and grasp the patient's arms, and hug the large root of the scapula, and extend it outward quite strongly: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot compress it in the way we have said, it is necessary that you bind the patient's two feet together with a strong soft strap on the two heels, and on the two shins, and the sick leg should be extended two thumbs more than the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then be hung on the top of a beam, and be two arms length above the ground; then command one attendant to grasp the patient's head, and have another attendant hanging with the patient, who grasps firmly the scapula, because the joint returns now quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at an end, have the patient lie down, as we have said in the case of hip joint, and stretch one strap on the sick leg properly, and on the thigh also.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then put two torches, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one torch between the patient's scapulae in the shape of an "L".
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and have damp cloths planted around, so that the patient is not harmed, then stretch out each attendant towards him, and the physician should place his hand on the joint of the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns to its place, that's good. If not, put the patient on a table and press in the same way as we have said for hip joint, and let the patient lie on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front of you, it's necessary to extend the sick leg quickly, and according to what I've said; and have the physician place his hand on the angle of the dislocated bone, then press with the other hand, and push downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is behind, it's not necessary to extend the sick leg downwards, nor lift it up towards the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated behind, in the same way that we have said for lying on both hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and be on its back, and the strap extended as we have said before, and it must compress on the joint at the table.
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be done when the patient stretches out their legs and they will be equal; then join the scapulae together, and apply a splint, and tie with a bandage, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and if the patient rests for 3 or 4 days, then remove the splint and apply a new one on top; and if you see that they are equal, tie it again as before, and leave it like that for 3 days; then remove it and let the patient move slowly, until the member is comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Let's move on to a new topic.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inwardly, outwardly, and behind; and do not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg to his knee, and if it does not bend to its knee, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit up straight, and stretch his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take his knee to your palms, and draw it between your two fists, then bend the two sides of the knee together; and another assistant stretches his foot, so that the joint returns to its place, and the sign is that he bends his leg lightly to his knee.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and put the plaster on it, and make him bend his leg to his knee, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, then unloose him; and do not let the patient get up, until the member is comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the member is not well, administer stretching strongly, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	It seems we've moved on to a new topic!
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The toes are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated within and without.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs of it are that the leg is swollen, and tense before the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	the return to its place is easy, and one must stretch it lightly with their hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is completely dislocated, you should have the patient sit upright, and rest on one leg, i.e., lean on a support with his foot above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take hold of the foot with your right hand and then with your left two times, then stretch it upwards, and firmly push up the foot upwards;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this two times, as we have said, by pushing and taking hold of the foot; if it returns, it's well; if not, then start over with the work, because it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in this way, then have the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place one strong stick firmly on the ground between his thighs, and bind cloths around him, so he does not harm himself;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then tie the stick between his thighs, and have another person stretch out the foot to their hands or on a rope, so that they can bind it above the ankle of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then have each person stretch equally, and the stick should be placed between the thighs of the patient in order to hold the patient when you stretch it.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then have the doctors on either side of the dislocation put their hands in place, and have another person tie the healthy leg to the lower part of it, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is back in place, you should apply an ointment and bandage over it, and form a splint, and tie the foot to the leg, and take care of the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the bandages are not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then let it be for two or three days, and if the bandages become loose, then rebandage it. Then release it on the third day or on the fourth, and prevent the patient from walking for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if he walks before this time is up, it's not a surety that it won't dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes up, you should treat it, just as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	It seems like the text has ended! Would you like to continue with another excerpt or start a new conversation?
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be nicely stretched without much effort, and it's a relatively easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any of the joints of the back or foot, it is necessary that you have the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table entirely straight, and place your foot over this joint, then press firmly with your foot until it returns.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in the cure, since you are not wise in the art and you have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitying and merciful and slow, nor too bold:
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and apply at the beginning soothing remedies for the suppurating wound and let the patient in God's hand, if you do not see hope of healing:
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then cleanse the limb now to its true state, so that the suppurating abscess may come:
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is to its true state, then administer soothing remedies for the suppurating abscess, and cure the wound as it needs with drying ointments:
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a fracture along with the dislocation, and small bones are broken, then set the bones, and do what we have said in simple diseases:
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Explicit le romen de fisique	The end of the book on medicine.
